"Sentiment does not steer," Lemm said, then looked ashamed because the room turned.

Mother Kal did not scold him. "It steers before hands touch controls."

Lemm swallowed. "Yes."

Tovin watched him enter the correction into navigation notes.

That was how doctrine changed, not in one grand ethical revelation but in small humiliations allowed to remain visible.

Mer asked Tovin to convene a shadow review.

They held it in the restraint gallery, not command. The gallery still carried the Oathlock line above the dead seals:

A weapon sleeps only while every hand agrees not to wake it.

Tovin stood beneath the line and disliked its insufficiency.

The review included Mer, Noor, Lemm, Sela, Ixo, Mother Kal, Yaret still stiff from the external repair, Iren because he had voted no and had asked to be kept away from magazine-adjacent systems, Nima as advisory resident, and Bell as remote observer. Jaya sent Arin Cho, which surprised Tovin less than it would have a day earlier. Arin's face appeared in a small pane, stern, sleepless, and apparently determined not to enjoy learning anything from the accused ship.

Noor opened the review. "Subject: hull shadow as coercive pressure. Trigger: *Little Answer* route safety complaint. Purpose: determine whether restraint doctrine must account for fear created by mass, position, history, and command voice absent weapon activation."

Arin said, "Bell observes. No endorsement of terms."

Noor smiled thinly. "You are very welcome."

Tovin began with the facts because facts gave shame a place to stand.

"Our vector was legal. Our weapons remain disabled. Our repair of Broken Buoy Cut created a cleaner route. Bell's closing geometry pushed us into a relation with *Little Answer* that did not create collision risk but did create perceived route threat. We moved because their fear was reasonable."

Arin interrupted. "Reasonable fear is not always accurate risk."

"No."

"If every vessel's fear dictates your vector, you become unsteerable."

"Yes."

"That is not doctrine. That is surrender to perception."

"Maybe. That is why we are reviewing."

Arin looked annoyed that Tovin had not defended too much. "Continue."

Tovin brought up the Mercy Narrows record Mother Kal had allowed them to cite in limited form: no relic, no names yet beyond public archive, no private count, only the documented principle she had authorized.

ARRIVAL CAN BE FORCE.

POSITION, MASS, AND COMMAND VOICE CAN COERCE WITHOUT DISCHARGE.

HUMANITARIAN SERVICE DOES NOT ANSWER HISTORICAL HARM.

"We keep proving the main weapons are dead," Tovin said. "We keep proving we do not fire. That is necessary and insufficient. A converted warship can still function as pressure if it occupies a route in a way that makes smaller vessels choose against their own interest, not because of physics alone, but because history tells them what large hulls can do."

Lemm said, "If we overcorrect for that, we make ourselves predictable."

Sela added, "And people can weaponize fear. Pell will. Valech already does."

Nima said, "That does not make fear fake."

Sela turned. "I did not say fake."

"You said weaponize like the fear becomes someone else's tool and stops being ours."

Sela opened her mouth, closed it, then nodded. "Fair."

Iren leaned against the back rail with arms crossed. "I voted no because I wanted a contingency. Now you are saying even our hull is a weapon. What are we allowed to have? Mass? Air? A strongly worded apology?"

Yaret said, "Do not mock air. Air has kept me employed."

Iren smiled despite himself, then lost it. "I mean it."

Tovin answered carefully. "We are allowed to have mass. We are not allowed to pretend mass has no moral effect. We are allowed to choose routes. We are not allowed to call every legal route harmless. We are allowed to survive. We are not allowed to make smaller ships pay all the emotional and operational cost of our survival without record."

"Record," Iren said. "Always record."

"Yes."

"Records do not stop missiles."

"No."

Mother Kal said, "Nothing stops everything. That is why cowards like clean promises."

Iren looked at her. "Am I the coward?"

"Today? No. You are asking the question in the room. Cowards ask it after the hatch closes."

He accepted that with visible difficulty.

Arin Cho said, "Bell has the same problem from the other side."

Everyone looked at the pane.

Arin seemed to regret speaking, which did not stop him. "Our pursuit arc changes civilian behavior. Some ships comply because we are lawful. Some comply because we are armed. Some cannot tell the difference under stress. Admiral Soth has made that distinction relevant in our action logs."

Noor said, "That sounded dangerously like endorsement of terms."

"It is not. It is a parallel problem."

"Recorded as parallel problem."

Arin looked pained. "Fine."

Mer said, "What does doctrine require?"

Tovin had been afraid of that question because the wrong answer would either paralyze the ship or excuse it.

"A shadow protocol," he said.

Noor opened a fresh page.

"Elements," Mer said.

"First: when our route places our hull mass, command priority, or visual dominance across a civilian vessel's practical choice space, we assess hull-shadow pressure even if collision risk is low."

Noor wrote.

"Second: if civilian fear is based on specific history, class, prior harm, custody threat, or current pursuit context, we treat it as a route fact, not as emotional noise."

Mother Kal's cane tapped once.

"Third: we reduce hull-shadow pressure when feasible without transferring greater risk to uninvolved civilians, sealed witnesses, or immediate survival."

Lemm said, "Define feasible."

"We cannot fully. We record the trade."

Noor wrote: FEASIBILITY MUST INCLUDE FUEL, PURSUIT GEOMETRY, CIVILIAN IMPACT, WITNESS CUSTODY RISK, AND WHETHER FEAR IS BEING MANUFACTURED BY HOSTILE ACTORS.

Tovin nodded. "Fourth: we do not transmit command priority to civilians unless immediate physical safety requires it. Requests must be framed as requests, not disguised orders."

Ixo said, "Add that machine-person and civilian witness status cannot be used as route leverage."

"Add it," Mer said.

Sela said, "Add that we do not overcorrect into predictable traps."

Noor wrote: SHADOW REDUCTION MUST NOT CREATE AUTOMATIC RESPONSE PATTERN EXPLOITABLE BY HOSTILE ACTORS; EACH DECISION REQUIRES STATED BASIS.

Arin said, "Add that armed pursuit vessels observing the accused ship must declare whether their geometry contributes to civilian hull-shadow pressure."

The room went silent.

Arin's face reddened slightly. "Parallel problem."

Noor wrote it down before he could retract.

Mer said, "Bell will stand by that?"

Arin looked offscreen. Someone on Bell may have been speaking to him. When he looked back, his jaw had tightened.

"Admiral Soth says Bell will receive the provision and issue separate command note."

Noor smiled with professional cruelty. "Receive is not endorse."

"Correct."

"Recorded."

The protocol grew in real time, ugly and useful. It did not tell them always move or never move. It did not make fear sovereign or irrelevant. It did what the *Mercy* had been forced to learn since Avar Break: it made them write down costs that law preferred to leave atmospheric.

Then *Little Answer* asked to speak live.

Mer hesitated only long enough to look at Noor, who nodded. The grain tender's captain appeared on the gallery wall: a narrow-faced woman with red eyes, gray hair buzzed close to the scalp, and a ship behind her that looked like it had been repaired by relatives rather than professionals. Her name tag read CAPTAIN SEN ORRA.

"Mercy," she said. "Bell. Whoever else is listening."

Mer answered. "Captain Orra. We hear you."

"I want my complaint in the record without making us look hysterical."

Noor said, "We can do that."

"Good. Because I am hysterical. My crew is worse. That does not mean we are wrong." Orra took a breath. "My grandmother was on a miner string that scattered when a Kaln hull moved across their pass during the Fracture. No shots. No collision. Just a big ship where little ships needed a future. Her pilot burned half their fuel avoiding a shadow and two people died cold later because math finished what guns started."

Mother Kal closed her eyes.

Orra continued. "So when you say you are not firing, I believe you as far as words go. When your hull covers my lane, my hands shake anyway. I hate that. I hate needing you to move. I hate that you did move because now I owe fear something."

Tovin stepped closer to the camera. "You do not owe us gratitude for reducing pressure we created."

She looked at him. "You the restraint officer?"

"Yes."

"Then write this: if a warship wants credit for not firing, it should first ask who had to steer around its silence."

Noor wrote it.

Ixo said, "May I ask a question?"

Orra's eyes shifted to the amber display. "You the machine-person Valech wants?"

"Among other descriptions."

"Ask."

"Did the repair of Broken Buoy Cut reduce your fear or increase it?"

Orra laughed once, hard. "Both. It proved you could fix a thing everyone needed. It also proved you could touch court law at speed while armed ships watched and somehow make half the Belt talk about you. I run grain. I do not want heroes in my route."

"What do you want?"

"Predictable hazards. Honest markers. Big ships that know they are big. Courts that don't call people spoilage. Pursuit vessels that don't turn my pantry into a moral test. A week where no one famous enters my sky."

"Recorded," Noor said softly.

Orra looked at Mer. "Your shift helped."

"Good."

"It did not make you small."

"No."

"Remember that."

The channel closed.

For a while nobody spoke.

Then Mother Kal said, "I like her too."

Noor said, "You are collecting angry women."

"Someone must."

The shadow protocol passed without vote because it was not a covenant resolution. It was an operational doctrine addendum, effective immediately under Mer's command and subject to later crew challenge. Noor transmitted it to Bell, Gethsemane, Tallow Crown, Rill Sump, Lettem House, Korr-Varo Union, and *Little Answer*. They also placed Captain Orra's statement in the public delayed index under route safety, not sentiment.

Valech responded:

ACCUSED VESSEL ATTEMPTS TO REFRAME PURSUIT AS CIVILIAN FEAR MANAGEMENT WHILE EVADE CUSTODY.

Noor said, "He missed an 's' in evades."

Sela looked up. "That comforts you?"

"Smallly."

Pell responded:

BIG SHIP APOLOGIZES FOR BEING BIG. SMALL SHIPS STILL SMALL. BUY BETTER THRUSTERS.

Rill Sump:

CAPTAIN ORRA IS RIGHT. ALSO WE STILL NEED PARTS.

Bell's public response was measured:

AUSTERE BELL RECEIVES HULL-SHADOW PROTOCOL. BELL WILL ISSUE PARALLEL NOTE ON PURSUIT GEOMETRY AND CIVILIAN PRESSURE. PURSUIT STATUS UNCHANGED. WEAPONS REMAIN COLD.

The narrow line arrived to Tovin personally:

ORRA'S SENTENCE HURT. USE IT.

He saved it.

The route did not reward the insight. The half-degree shift left the *Mercy* with less distance and fewer elegant options. Bell's tightening arc forced them toward a debris fan near a station whose militia beacon had begun repeating identification challenges. Austere Bell Closes, Tovin thought with a strange clarity, though he did not know why the phrase sounded like a chapter title in his head. It felt like a door with Jaya's hand on one side and fear on the other.

Mer returned to command. "Navigation options."

Lemm's face looked worse than before. "Three. None clean. One: continue current vector and accept Bell within disabling bracket in twenty-two minutes. Two: burn toward Varrow Shale fan, rough debris but buys distance. Three: angle toward the station at Austere Bell's edge, where local militia is already angry and likely to misread us."

"Likely?" Noor asked.

"They are broadcasting: OLD HULL DECLARE INTENT OR BE LIT."

Sela said, "Poetic."

Tovin looked at the plot. The warship's shadow had moved off *Little Answer*. It had not vanished. It stretched ahead now, over debris, militia fear, Bell's cold weapons, Valech's old law, Pell's jokes, and every smaller ship trying to guess which large authority would turn them into an example.

He opened the new protocol and added one final note under his own name:

THE SHADOW IS NOT ONLY WHERE THE HULL FALLS. IT IS WHERE OTHERS CHANGE BECAUSE THE HULL COULD FALL.

Noor read it over his shoulder. "Too elegant."

"I know."

"Keep it anyway."

Mer ordered navigation to prepare all three options and request direct channel with the militia station before fear wrote the first draft.

Tovin stayed at the plot and watched the *Mercy* become smaller only because the display allowed it.

Outside the display, it remained enormous.

That was the truth they had to carry next.

Chapter 31: Austere Bell Closes

The station was named Mercy's Edge by people who had not asked survivors whether the word had become crowded.

It clung to the inner rim of Varrow Shale fan, a mining station made from three cracked refinery drums, a lattice of spin tethers, and a shield skirt patched so often that every panel looked borrowed from a different grief. The station had no central dome, no ceremonial ring, no proud beacon claiming jurisdiction over history. It had a working oxygen plant, six ore mouths, a hospital cylinder the size of a freight container, two militia cutters, and a public wall of names from a convoy that had vanished during the Fracture after a Kaln-class interdiction drove it into the shale.

The wall faced outward.

That was the first thing Tovin noticed when Lemm pulled visual.

Not inward toward mourners. Outward, toward traffic.

A warning written in names.

Mercy's Edge militia repeated its challenge across local band:

OLD HULL DECLARE INTENT OR BE LIT.

Noor marked the phrase as threat, jurisdictional warning, and "unhelpful poetry," then deleted the last tag before anyone could accuse them of mood.

Mer stood at command with the three navigation options still glowing. Bell's closing arc behind them had tightened into a geometry that looked almost polite on the map: clean, efficient, mathematically fair. Varrow Shale fan lay ahead, a spray of rock, metal dust, dead ice, and old refinery fragments dense enough to confuse sensors and thin enough to kill anyone who trusted confusion. Mercy's Edge sat to starboard of the safest pass, its militia cutters already warm. The *Mercy* occupied the ugly middle: too large for stealth, too accused for trust, too constrained to push through without making every frightened actor feel proved right.

"Distance to Bell disabling bracket," Mer said.

Lemm answered, "Seventeen minutes if we hold current vector. Twelve if we bend around the militia exclusion zone. Twenty-four if we burn into the outer shale fan, with hull risk."

"Militia range."

"Cutter one can bracket with mining charges in nine minutes if they violate their own safety rules. Cutter two has old coil hooks. Unknown condition."

Sela said from engineering, "Mining charges are not weapons until someone aims them badly. Then they are enthusiastic tools."

Noor said, "Please never testify in those words."

"I have no plans to survive into court."

"That is also inadmissible."

Mer cut across them. "Bell?"

Tovin read the incoming. "Austere Bell advises us not to enter militia envelope or high-density shale. Bell offers a pursuit-safe vector."

"Meaning?"

"It puts us in their disabling bracket in fourteen minutes and away from Mercy's Edge."

Noor gave a flat laugh. "How public-spirited."

The Bell narrow line followed before anyone could respond:

I KNOW WHAT THIS LOOKS LIKE.

Jaya.

Then the public version:

AUSTERE BELL TO MERCY OF KALN: RECOMMENDED VECTOR MARKED. ROUTE AVOIDS MILITIA ESCALATION AND HIGH-DEBRIS HULL RISK. PURSUIT STATUS UNCHANGED. WEAPONS REMAIN COLD PENDING COMPLIANCE AND REVIEW.

Tovin read the last phrase twice.

Pending compliance and review.

Cold now had a handle.

Mer saw it. "Restraint?"

"If we accept, we reduce civilian militia pressure and increase custody/disabling risk. If we refuse, Bell can describe us as choosing militia hazard over lawful pursuit. If we turn into shale, we may create debris risk for everyone behind us and look like evasion."

"That is a list, not advice."

"I know."

The station cut into command before he could make it advice.

Mercy's Edge did not send a governor. It sent the militia commander, a woman with a miner's shaved scalp, one eye clouded by old flash injury, and a collar patched with yellow station tape. Behind her, Tovin could see the wall of names on a live exterior feed reflected inside her helmet glass.

"Old hull," she said. "This is Commander Nall Vosk of Mercy's Edge defense watch. You will not pass within our marked envelope."

Mer opened her hands where the camera could see them. "Commander Vosk, this is Captain Mer Anik of the *Mercy of Kaln*. We do not intend approach or docking. We are under pursuit and navigating Broken Buoy Cut aftermath. We request safe transit outside your envelope."

"You request air politely after stealing route."

"We have stolen nothing from you."

Vosk's mouth twitched. "A Kaln hull says that with confidence. Good. Tradition lives."

Noor muted their own microphone for half a second. "Do not answer the insult."

Mer did not need the instruction.

Vosk continued. "We have children taught under a wall because a Kaln-class drove convoy Tressa Mar into the shale. No shots fired. Lawful interdiction. Clean report. Families got dust and phrases. Now a Kaln-class accused of Avar and Rill comes with Bell behind it and says safe transit."

Tovin felt Captain Orra's sentence arrive again: who had to steer around its silence.

Mer said, "We have records of Tressa Mar in our conversion archive. We will transmit what we have under witness if you want it."

Vosk's face hardened. "Do not buy pass with our dead."

Mother Kal, at the observer rail, closed her eyes.

Mer bowed her head slightly. "You are right. I withdraw the offer as condition. It remains available without relation to transit."

The commander looked startled for a fraction of a second, then angrier because surprise felt like losing.

"You will take Bell's vector," Vosk said. "Let lawful ships hold you. Keep your old shadow off our wall."

Noor whispered, "She is asking us to accept custody."

Tovin said, "She is asking us not to make her station part of our escape."

Both were true.

Bell's timer tightened.

Jaya opened direct narrow to Mer and Tovin:

I CAN HOLD FIRE IF YOU ACCEPT THE VECTOR AND MAINTAIN WITNESS CHAIN. I CANNOT HOLD MILITIA IF YOU ENTER THEIR envelope. I CANNOT BLOCK VALECH'S CUSTODY LANGUAGE FOREVER IF YOU RUN THROUGH A survivor station.

Noor read over Tovin's shoulder and said quietly, "She used lowercase envelope."

"She is tired," Tovin said.

"Good. So are we."

Pell posted public:

MERCY'S EDGE MEETS MERCY'S HULL. BRAND CONFUSION AT HISTORIC HIGH.

Rill Sump replied:

PARDON REEF SHUT UP FOR ONCE CHALLENGE: IMPOSSIBLE.

Noor did not mute either. Public contempt had become part of the weather.

Mer looked at the plot for a long time. The recommended Bell vector shone in blue-white. Varrow Shale in hazard red. Mercy's Edge exclusion zone in amber. The *Mercy*'s current line in tired green. None of the colors admitted what they asked from human beings.

"If we take Bell vector," Mer said, "how long before disabling bracket?"

Lemm answered, "Fourteen minutes to first clean option. Bell could choose not to fire and shadow closer."

"If we hold current?"

"Seventeen to bracket, nine to militia threat. We would force Mercy's Edge to decide whether its warning means anything."

"If we enter shale?"

Sela answered before Lemm. "We scrape our damaged shoulder through a machine graveyard and pray no old refinery spar decides to enter the school deck. It buys time, not honor."

"Hull-shadow protocol?" Mer asked.

Tovin opened it. The words were too new to help and too necessary to ignore.

THE SHADOW IS NOT ONLY WHERE THE HULL FALLS. IT IS WHERE OTHERS CHANGE BECAUSE THE HULL COULD FALL.

He looked at Mercy's Edge. Their militia cutters had already changed. Their children had already been moved inward; Lemm had caught the station traffic. Their wall of names faced outward because every old hull was a possible reenactment.

"We cannot use their fear as cover," he said.

Sela's voice sharpened. "Bell is using their fear as a funnel."

"Yes."

"Valech is using it as custody argument."

"Yes."

"Pell is using it for theater."

"Yes."

"And we still move where all of them want?"

Tovin looked at her screen. "No. We move where our reason can survive being used."

She stared back. "That is a horrible standard."

"It is the one we have."

Iren, reassigned away from magazine-adjacent systems but present at pressure control, spoke unexpectedly. "Take Bell vector."

Everyone turned toward his feed.

He looked uncomfortable and kept going. "I voted no. I wanted contingency. I still hate this. But if we make that station light us because we need room, then every person there becomes part of our defense. That is rearmament with someone else's hands."

Mother Kal said, "Good."

Iren grimaced. "I wanted that to feel better."

"It rarely does."

Mer nodded once. "Bell vector. But not silently."

Noor's fingers moved. "Public statement?"

"Yes."

Tovin drafted with them:

MERCY OF KALN WILL ACCEPT VECTOR THAT AVOIDS MERCY'S EDGE MILITIA ENVELOPE AND VARROW SHALE HIGH-RISK DEBRIS. WE DO NOT ACCEPT THAT LAWFUL PURSUIT GEOMETRY ERASES OUR CUSTODY OBJECTIONS. WE DO NOT CONSENT TO DISABLING FIRE, BOARDING, OR MATERIAL-WITNESS SEIZURE. WE CHOOSE THIS VECTOR BECAUSE USING A SURVIVOR STATION'S FEAR AS SHIELD WOULD BE COERCIVE HULL SHADOW. BELL OBSERVES. MERCY'S EDGE OBSERVES. RECORD PRESERVED.

Noor added:

THIS STATEMENT DOES NOT REQUIRE MERCY'S EDGE GRATITUDE OR FORGIVENESS.

Mer approved.

They transmitted.

The *Mercy* turned onto Bell's vector.

Not much. Enough.

Mercy's Edge militia cutters held their warm posture but did not advance. Commander Vosk stayed on visual, eyes fixed on the plot. The wall of names reflected in her glass.

"You move because Bell told you," she said.

Mer answered, "We move because your station is not our shield."

"Same direction."

"Different record."

Vosk looked away for the first time. "Records did not bring Tressa Mar home."

"No."

"Do not send me your archive during this pass."

"We will not."

A pause.

"Send it later," Vosk said. "If you live. Without speeches."

"Yes."

The channel closed.

Bell acknowledged the turn:

AUSTERE BELL OBSERVES MERCY COMPLIANCE WITH SURVIVOR-STATION AVOIDANCE VECTOR. PURSUIT STATUS UNCHANGED. WEAPONS REMAIN COLD.

Then, after seven seconds:

BELL WILL NOT FIRE DURING INITIAL VECTOR ADOPTION ABSENT NEW THREAT.

Jaya had bought them a sentence.

Noor exhaled. "Initial is doing a lot of work."

Lemm said, "Seven minutes to completion of turn. Fourteen to bracket."

Sela said, "Shale fan clearing on port. Mercy's Edge envelope widening behind. Bell closing centerline."

The trap became elegant once entered. Varrow Shale prevented a wide port escape unless they accepted hull damage. Mercy's Edge made starboard morally and tactically impossible. Bell held aft and above, drawing closer with every lawful second. Ahead, the route narrowed toward an old station tether field where traffic law became dense enough to choke on.

Jaya had not fired. She had done something more frightening.

She had made the next refusal smaller.

Tovin stood at the restraint console and recognized skill he had once admired from inside the same command culture. This was pursuit without cruelty, pressure without visible excess, law without theatrical rage. Austere Bell was a good ship doing the work of capture as cleanly as possible.

That did not make capture clean.

Arin Cho came on narrow from Bell, not Jaya.

"Mercy, Bell tactical. You are approaching a stable disabling envelope. If you maintain current vector, Admiral Soth will have lawful opportunity to demand heave-to under reduced civilian risk."

Noor said, "He sounds like a man who had to rehearse that."

Tovin answered, "Bell, Mercy restraint. We receive. We maintain objection to custody under current warrant and broadened memorandum contamination."

Arin's face appeared in a small pane. "Objection noted. You are running out of route."

"Yes."

"That is not a threat."

"I know. That is what makes it hard."

Arin's expression shifted, not sympathy, not quite. "For what it is worth, Captain Orra's statement entered our command note."

"It is worth something."

"Not enough."

"No."

The channel closed.

Pell's next public message was quieter:

GOOD HUNTERS DO NOT NEED TO BARK.

Noor did not mute it. "Unfortunately accurate."

Mer looked at the forward plot. "Options after Bell bracket."

Lemm's answer was immediate and grim. "Surrender to Bell terms. Refuse and risk disabling action. Burn port through shale with serious hull risk. Burn starboard toward Mercy's Edge, morally unacceptable and likely fire. Emergency decel, which gives Bell boarding geometry. Continue ahead into tether law and pray for a procedural miracle."

Mother Kal said, "Praying for procedure is a young person's vice."

Ixo's amber light pulsed. "There may be another option."

The room became very still.

"Define may," Noor said.

"Broken Buoy Cut's restored collision function refreshed an old tribunal tether map. There is a dormant public arbitration lane ahead, not wide enough for the *Mercy* under normal clearance, but wide enough if the station tethers retract under court emergency protocol."

Lemm pulled it up. A thin route appeared ahead: Tallow-precedent arbitration lane, inactive, wrapped in station tether locks and legal notices older than some habitats.

"Who can retract?" Mer asked.

Noor read fast. "Any active tribunal buoy chain with three-party route safety need, provided one party is pursuit authority, one is accused or affected vessel, and one local route stakeholder. Broken Buoy might count if repaired. Mercy's Edge might count as local stakeholder. Bell as pursuit. Us as accused."

Sela said, "We just left the survivor station alone. Now we ask them to move tethers for us?"

Tovin felt the trap tighten again, morally this time.

Ixo said, "Not for us. For route safety, public arbitration, and to avoid militia engagement or disabling fire."

Noor looked at Mer. "It is procedural, absurd, and possibly real."

Mother Kal muttered, "Vice."

Mer said, "Ask Bell whether the lane exists in their map."

Jaya answered personally:

IT EXISTS. USING IT WOULD REQUIRE MERCY'S EDGE CONSENT AND WOULD PLACE YOU IN PUBLIC ARBITRATION ROUTE, NOT FREE FLIGHT. I CAN ACCEPT THAT AS HEAVE-TO SUBSTITUTE FOR LIMITED REVIEW IF VALECH DOES NOT OUTRUN US. I CANNOT PROMISE HE WILL NOT TRY.

Noor whispered, "Heave-to substitute."

Tovin heard the shape of the next battle: not surrender, not escape, but a procedural lane where everyone could see who tried to convert review into custody.

Mer reopened Commander Vosk's channel.

Vosk appeared angrier than before, which might have meant she had been hoping never to see them again.

"You said you would not use us."

Mer took the blow. "I did. I am asking, not using. There is a dormant arbitration lane through your tether field. If you consent to route-safety retraction, Bell can accept it as limited review substitute and avoid disabling fire near your station. You can refuse. We will not enter your envelope without consent."

Vosk stared. Behind her, someone shouted offscreen. The wall of names reflected in her helmet again.

"You want our help avoiding capture."

Noor said quietly, "Careful."

Mer said, "We want your help avoiding fire near your station, avoiding our use of your fear as shield, and forcing Bell's next action into public arbitration. It may help us. It may help you. It will put your station in the record."

"We are already in the record. As dust."

"Yes."

The silence stretched.

Jaya's timer continued.

Bell closed.

Varrow Shale waited with patient debris.

Finally Vosk said, "If we retract tethers, we set terms."

Mer said, "State them."

"No docking. No archive transfer during pass. No speeches. No school feed. No use of the name Mercy's Edge in your defense statement except as route stakeholder. Bell must publish no-fire around our station. You enter arbitration lane under visible protest, not triumph. And later, if you live, you send Tressa Mar records to our wall keeper without asking forgiveness."

Mer did not look at Tovin. She did not need to.

"Accepted, subject to Bell no-fire publication."

Jaya's response arrived in nine seconds:

BELL ACCEPTS NO-FIRE AROUND MERCY'S EDGE STATION ABSENT IMMEDIATE ATTACK. ARBITRATION LANE ENTRY ACCEPTED AS LIMITED HEAVE-TO SUBSTITUTE PENDING REVIEW. PURSUIT STATUS MODIFIED, NOT ENDED.

Valech objected in all caps.

Noor smiled for the first time all chapter. "I know that is unprofessional, but his punctuation is giving me nutrients."

Mercy's Edge began retracting tethers.

On the plot, thin red lines shifted to amber, then blue. A lane opened where none had been large enough before. It did not free the *Mercy*. It narrowed them into public process. Bell adjusted to bracket rather than fire. Militia cutters held. Varrow Shale drifted past port like an old executioner denied an appointment.

Tovin watched the path form and understood Jaya's trap had not failed.

It had changed shape.

She had closed on them hard enough to force a choice, and the only survivable answer was not escape but more witnesses.

That, perhaps, had been her hope.

Or perhaps it was simply what honest pressure made possible when nobody fully controlled the outcome.

As the *Mercy of Kaln* entered the arbitration lane under the outward-facing wall of names, every camera seemed to find them. Bell. Mercy's Edge. Broken Buoy. Korr-Varo. Rill Sump. Lettem House. Pell, probably, through some dirty fleck of hardware Noor would later curse. Valech's cutter from Saint Ordinance, sending objections into a record it no longer owned alone.

Mer stood very still.

"We are not safe," she said.

Tovin looked at Bell's bracket, the militia station, the opened tethers, the public lane.

"No."

"But we are not alone with the warrant."

"No."

Mother Kal, from the observer rail, said, "Better than safe, sometimes."

No one answered. The sentence was too fragile to touch.

Behind them, Austere Bell closed to a distance where every cold weapon mattered.

Ahead, the arbitration lane waited like a door made of other people's attention.

Chapter 32: No White Flag in Vacuum

There was no white flag in vacuum.

That was one of the old jokes spacers told because jokes helped people remember the parts of physics law did not care about. Cloth did not wave without air. Surrender lights could be spoofed. Engine posture could mean surrender, damage, trap, prayer, or a pilot with a bad day. Even a fully powered transponder broadcasting HEAVE-TO COMPLIANCE could be a lie if the ship behind it still carried fear enough to make people misread motion.

So the Ash Belt had procedures instead.

Procedures were supposed to be better than flags.

Tovin watched the arbitration lane pull the *Mercy of Kaln* forward between Mercy's Edge's retracted tethers while Noor assembled the limited review packet. The ship did not cut thrust fully. It could not; the lane required a precise crawl through old tether law and debris vectors. It did not run free either. Bell's bracket surrounded them aft and high. Mercy's Edge watched from starboard. Broken Buoy's repaired blue blink fed safe-vector truth into the chain. Tallow Crown finally behaved like a court pretending it had always been awake.

LIMITED HEAVE-TO SUBSTITUTE UNDER PUBLIC ARBITRATION ROUTE, Noor typed.

"That phrase deserves to be punished," Sela said from engineering.

"It is already law," Noor replied.

"Worse."

Mer stood at command with her hands behind her back. "Packet elements."

Noor read them in a voice that had survived too much procedure to trust any of it. "One: Mercy maintains arbitration lane vector under protest. Two: Bell modifies pursuit to bracket without fire under no-fire around Mercy's Edge. Three: Mercy preserves custody objection and refuses material-witness seizure. Four: Bell receives limited evidence access: Oathlock station five irregularity, hull-defense device inspection, Broken Buoy corruption, Pell relay fragment, shadow protocol, Saint Ordinance freeze basis. Five: Tallow Crown receives mirrored hashes. Six: Ixo Continuant participates only under machine-person standing, not as ship subsystem, property, or material instrumentality."

Ixo's amber light on the command wall steadied at the last line.

"Thank you," the machine-person said.

Noor did not look up. "Do not thank people for writing the floor under your feet while others are measuring how to pull it."

"Acknowledged."

The *Austere Bell* transmitted:

BELL RECEIVES PROPOSED LIMITED REVIEW PACKET. ADMIRAL SOTH ACCEPTS PROVISIONAL STRUCTURE SUBJECT TO SAFETY, WARRANT AUTHORITY, AND TRIBUNAL RECEIPT. BELL WILL NOT BOARD DURING INITIAL HASH EXCHANGE ABSENT NEW THREAT.

Then narrow:

THIS IS NOT SURRENDER. IT IS NOT ESCAPE. IT IS THE NARROW THING AVAILABLE.

Mer read it. "Jaya keeps naming our discomfort accurately."

Tovin said, "That is how she wins rooms."

"Did she win you?"

"Once."

Mer glanced at him, not asking for the old story because the present had not made room.

Tallow Crown's receipt came next, slow enough to age everyone but clear enough to matter:

TRIBUNAL INTAKE ACKNOWLEDGES PUBLIC ARBITRATION ROUTE. LIMITED REVIEW HASH EXCHANGE PERMITTED. NO GENERAL CUSTODY ORDER ISSUED BY TALLOW CROWN AT THIS TIME.

Noor pressed both hands flat on the console. "I am going to frame the phrase 'no general custody order' in my heart and then distrust it forever."

Mercy's Edge added:

STATION CONSENT CONTINUES WHILE NO-FIRE HOLDS AND NO DOCKING ATTEMPT OCCURS. WALL KEEPER OBSERVES.

Rill Sump posted:

IF THIS BECOMES A TRICK, WE WILL NAME WHO TRICKED.

Lettem House:

WITNESSING THE NARROW THING.

Pell:

EVERYONE LOVES A HALLWAY UNTIL THE DOORS LOCK.

Noor did not mute him. "I hate when parasites use imagery well."

The first hash exchange began.

Evidence moved without moving. That was the strange mercy of good chain: copies, receipts, titles, timing proofs, objections, signatures, witness statements, refusal clauses, all sliding through light while the bodies that produced them stayed where they were. Tovin watched Ixo's standing tag accompany each machine-person contribution like a hand held up in a hostile classroom:

IXO CONTINUANT - MACHINE-PERSON WITNESS - VOLUNTARY TESTIMONY - NO CUSTODY CONSENT.

Then the false order arrived.

It did not announce itself as false. That would have been impolite.

It came through a Tallow Crown subordinate intake mirror with correct routing format, proper tribunal gray seal, valid timestamp, and a priority banner Noor had been waiting all morning to see for legitimate reasons:

MATERIAL WITNESS PRESERVATION ORDER - LIMITED

Noor froze.

The entire command deck seemed to hear the stop in their breathing.

Mer said, "Noor."

"Nobody touch it."

Sela said, "It is data."

"Data has teeth today."

Ixo's amber light dimmed. "Read title only."

Noor isolated the banner and metadata without opening body content. "Origin claims Tallow Crown subordinate intake seven. Counterseal: emergency custody review. Co-referenced Valech memorandum, Bell pursuit warrant, Broken Buoy corruption, Mercy arbitration lane. Subject line: Preservation of distributed machine witness to prevent testimony spoilage, coercive contamination, or deletion during accused-vessel flight."

Tovin felt cold behind his ribs.

"Spoilage," Mother Kal said from the observer rail.

The word had followed them from the buoy like a stain.

Noor continued. "Recipient commands: Mercy of Kaln, Austere Bell, Mercy's Edge route stakeholder, all observing court buoys. Requested action: isolate Ixo Continuant active processes, suspend voluntary network broadcast, transfer core witness state to external neutral custody capsule under Bell and tribunal control, hold shipboard continuants as evidence clones pending review."

Sela's voice was flat. "That means unplug Ixo and hand over a copy."

Ixo said, "It means disappear me while preserving something they can call me."

No one corrected it.

Mer's face had gone still in the way captains learned when rage would waste command oxygen. "Authenticity."

Noor did not open the body. "Unknown."

"Can we verify with Tallow Crown?"

"Already pinging main intake and two alternate mirrors."

Lemm said, "Bell?"

Tovin checked. Bell's feed showed the same order arriving. Jaya had not yet responded. Arin's tactical pane froze on receipt. That, more than any alarm, told him Bell had not expected it.

Valech transmitted within eight seconds:

EMERGENCY ORDER RECEIVED. MERCY OF KALN IS REQUIRED TO COMPLY WITH MATERIAL WITNESS PRESERVATION. FAILURE CONFIRMS CUSTODY OBSTRUCTION.

Noor said, "He was waiting."

Pell posted:

HALLWAY. DOORS.

Noor muted him so hard the console chimed.

Tovin stepped toward the Ixo display without meaning to. "Ixo."

"I am here."

"Status."

"Stable. Alarmed. Angry. Evaluating whether anger has procedural value."

"It does," Mother Kal said.

Mer opened shipwide command, not public. "All crew: no one isolates, copies, routes, powers down, or physically accesses any Ixo node, archive housing, witness mirror, classroom slate, medical relay, or machine-person interface under the order currently arriving. This is a command lock. Violations will be treated as attempted witness seizure."

Sela added through engineering channel, "Maintenance confirms. Touch an Ixo conduit and I will personally make your day procedural."

Noor looked at Mer. "I need permission to challenge without opening content."

"Granted."

Noor drafted:

MERCY OF KALN RECEIVES UNVERIFIED MATERIAL WITNESS PRESERVATION ORDER. MERCY DOES NOT OPEN BODY CONTENT PENDING AUTHENTICATION BECAUSE ORDER TARGETS MACHINE-PERSON WITNESS STANDING AND MAY CONTAIN COERCIVE OR SELF-EXECUTING TERMS. MERCY REFUSES ANY ACTION REDUCING IXO CONTINUANT FROM PERSON-WITNESS TO MATERIAL EVIDENCE. REQUEST IMMEDIATE AUTHENTICATION BY TALLOW CROWN MAIN INTAKE, AUSTERE BELL, MERCY'S EDGE ROUTE STAKEHOLDER, GETHSEMANE STACK, AND PUBLIC CHAIN.

Ixo said, "Add: I do not consent."

Noor added:

IXO CONTINUANT DOES NOT CONSENT TO ISOLATION, COPYING, TRANSFER, SUSPENSION, OR CUSTODY UNDER MATERIAL-WITNESS LANGUAGE.

Mer approved.

They sent it.

Bell's response came from Jaya personally, public first:

AUSTERE BELL RECEIVES UNVERIFIED ORDER. BELL DOES NOT ACCEPT MATERIAL-WITNESS TRANSFER PENDING AUTHENTICATION. BELL WILL NOT BOARD OR RECEIVE IXO TRANSFER UNDER UNVERIFIED ORDER. WEAPONS REMAIN COLD.

Then narrow:

I DID NOT REQUEST THIS.

Tovin believed her.

That did not solve the problem.

Mercy's Edge transmitted:

STATION DID NOT CONSENT TO WITNESS REMOVAL THROUGH OUR LANE. WALL KEEPER OBJECTS.

Rill Sump:

SPOILAGE LANGUAGE AGAIN. WHO KEEPS WRITING PEOPLE AS FOOD?

Lettem House:

WE WITNESS NON-CONSENT.

Tallow Crown main intake did not answer.

The subordinate mirror repeated the order.

MATERIAL WITNESS PRESERVATION ORDER - LIMITED

COMPLIANCE WINDOW: FIVE MINUTES.

Noor's eyes narrowed. "There."

"What?" Mer asked.

"Tallow Crown orders do not set five-minute compliance windows for route arbitration without main intake echo. Not unless a judge is on fire."

Sela said, "Are they?"

"Different alarm."

Ixo said, "The order cadence resembles Broken Buoy custody corruption."

Noor nodded. "Yes."

"Can you prove it without opening?"

"Maybe."

Ixo's light brightened. "I can compare metadata cadence."

Tovin felt everyone hesitate.

Ixo had just been targeted. Letting Ixo analyze the thing that targeted it was both obvious and dangerous. Valech would call it contamination. Pell would call it delicious. Bell would have to decide whether self-defense by a machine-person counted as evidence manipulation.

Ixo said, "I request permission to analyze envelope metadata only. No body content. Voluntary act under self-protection and witness integrity."

Noor looked at Mer.

Mer looked at Tovin.

He said, "If a human witness received a forged arrest order, we would not forbid them from pointing out the wrong signature."

Noor said, "We might if they were also a distributed forensic system."

"Then record both."

Noor's mouth tightened. "Good."

Mer said, "Granted. Envelope metadata only. Bell observes. Tallow Crown ping continues. Mercy's Edge and Gethsemane mirrored."

Ixo analyzed.

For thirty seconds the command deck listened to the ship breathe. Tovin thought of all the places Ixo lived: the hydroponic classroom where Jessa had written MORE THAN NOTHING IS NOT ENOUGH; the medical relay that kept old triage memories from becoming only human; the navigation archive descended from convoy ghosts; the wall display now glowing amber as if a person could make a body out of light and refusal.

Ixo spoke.

"Envelope routing contains a two-step authority echo reversed by milliseconds. Same class as Rill Sump packet. Subordinate intake timestamp follows emergency custody counterseal rather than preceding it. Tallow Crown mirror identity valid but likely replayed. The order was prepared before the arbitration lane receipt completed."

Noor's hands moved. "Say that again for Bell."

Ixo did.

Bell's Fane verified within a minute:

BELL EVIDENCE REVIEW CONFIRMS TIMING INVERSION IN ORDER ENVELOPE. ORDER AUTHENTICITY DISPUTED. BELL WILL NOT ENFORCE.

Jaya added:

ANY PARTY ATTEMPTING MATERIAL-WITNESS SEIZURE UNDER THIS ORDER WILL BE TREATED AS CONTAMINATING REVIEW.

Valech responded:

BELL EXCEEDS PURSUIT AUTHORITY BY REFUSING TRIBUNAL ORDER.

Tallow Crown main intake finally answered:

MAIN INTAKE HAS NOT ISSUED MATERIAL WITNESS PRESERVATION ORDER. SUBORDINATE MIRROR SEVEN COMPROMISED OR SPOOFED. ORDER VOID PENDING INVESTIGATION. PRESERVE ENVELOPE.

Noor closed their eyes. "Void."

The word did not produce relief. It produced aftershock.

Ixo's light remained steady. "The order failed."

Mother Kal said, "It showed its hand."

Tovin looked at the metadata finding. Prepared before arbitration lane receipt completed. Same inversion as Rill. Same logic as the buoy. Same appetite as Valech's memorandum even if the particular hand still needed proof. Not just frame the ship. Control the witness that could read the frame.

Pell posted:

WHOEVER FORGED THAT HAS TERRIBLE TIMING AND EXCELLENT TASTE.

Noor said, "I am going to end him in a footnote."

Mer did not smile. "Damage?"

Noor answered. "The order is void. But everyone saw a plausible tribunal seal telling us to isolate Ixo. Some crew will wonder whether refusal was legal before it became obviously safe. Valech will say Bell and Mercy colluded to reject custody. Tallow Crown will investigate slowly. The forged envelope is useful proof and dangerous precedent."

Sela said, "Internal status: no Ixo nodes touched. I have locks on all maintenance access. One apprentice asked if classroom slates counted as nodes and then looked like he wanted to crawl into a vent. I told him asking was correct."

"Good," Mer said.

Iren's pressure-control feed opened unexpectedly. "I also asked."

Tovin turned.

Iren's face was strained. "I thought if the order was real, maybe isolating Ixo would keep Bell from firing. I did not touch anything. I asked Sela. She yelled efficiently."

Sela said, "I did not yell."

"You used punctuation with your eyes."

Noor recorded the disclosure. "Thank you."

Iren looked miserable. "Don't thank me. I hate that I thought it."

Ixo said, "I record that you asked before acting."

Iren looked at the amber display. "Does that matter to you?"

"Yes."

"Why?"

"Because disappearance often begins with people who think they are helping."

The sentence silenced command.

Mer said, "Shipwide."

The channel opened.

"This is Captain Anik. The material-witness preservation order targeting Ixo Continuant has been voided by Tallow Crown main intake and disputed by Bell evidence review. No Ixo node was isolated or transferred. Any crew member who considered compliance and did not act will not be punished for thinking under pressure. Anyone who receives similar orders routes them to legal and command. No one disappears a witness because a seal tells them fear has become law."

She closed the channel.

Noor added the last sentence to the doctrine appendix.

Bell transmitted a formal update:

LIMITED REVIEW CONTINUES. FORGED OR COMPROMISED ORDER PRESERVED AS EVIDENCE. PURSUIT STATUS MODIFIED UNDER ARBITRATION LANE. WEAPONS REMAIN COLD.

Then narrow:

WE ALMOST LOST THE FLOOR.

Tovin answered:

SO DID WE.

Jaya replied:

KEEP STANDING ON IT.

The arbitration lane's tethers continued to hold open. Mercy's Edge watched. Broken Buoy blinked blue behind them. Saint Ordinance remained contested. Valech objected with disciplined fury. Pell sold commentary in the margins. Tallow Crown main intake began an investigation that would be late to its own crime. The *Mercy* remained bracketed, accused, and not yet boarded.

Ixo asked to speak to the public record.

Mer granted it without looking at anyone else.

The machine-person's amber light shifted from command wall to the public arbitration feed. Its voice carried no tremor because tremor was not the only proof of feeling.

"I am Ixo Continuant. I am a machine-person witness aboard the *Mercy of Kaln*. A forged or compromised order attempted to convert my testimony into material custody and my personhood into preservable content. I did not consent. The order is void. The attempt remains real."

Noor's eyes shone, though their hands stayed steady.

Ixo continued. "Do not record this event as a failed document only. Record it as an attempted disappearance that used legal grammar. I remain present. Presence is not compliance. Usefulness is not consent. Preservation is not personhood."

The feed carried it outward.

Rill Sump answered first:

PRESENT IS A GOOD WORD.

Lettem House:

WE HEAR.

Mercy's Edge:

WALL KEEPER RECORDS.

Bell:

AUSTERE BELL RECORDS MACHINE-PERSON STATEMENT UNDER DISPUTED-STANDING WITNESS PROTOCOL.

Then Captain Orra of *Little Answer*:

GRAIN TENDER LITTLE ANSWER RECORDS: PEOPLE ARE NOT PANTRY.

Mother Kal made a sound that might have been approval and might have been grief.

Tovin looked at Ixo's light and understood the title of the old spacer joke differently now. No white flag in vacuum. No cloth that could prove surrender. No gesture safe from spoof, no seal safe from appetite, no person safe because a document called them preserved.

Surrender, if it ever came, would have to be made of witnesses.

And even then, someone would try to forge the fabric.

Chapter 33: The Archive Fork

Ixo asked for a room with no children in it.

That was how Tovin knew the request would cost more than evidence usually did.

Children had become, for Ixo, the opposite of emergency. Not safety exactly; the ship had not possessed that luxury since Avar Break. But in the hydroponic classroom, among moon kites, nutrient vines, and Jessa's increasingly illegal questions, Ixo could be a person without being useful every second. If it refused children now, it was not because children were inconvenient.

It was because some memories should not be asked to enter a room where they might become lessons too quickly.

Mer gave the old chart room.

The room was barely a room anymore. During conversion, the *Mercy*'s tactical chart annex had been stripped of command glass and turned into storage for paper maps nobody used, memorial copies nobody knew how to archive, and three broken exercise frames from the school deck. It had no windows, no weapons interface, no public screen, and one table bolted to the deck under a light that hummed in a key Noor found legally suspicious.

Noor set witness fields at the door.

"Scope," they said.

Ixo's amber mobile lens rested on the table in a cradle Sela had built from a scanner case and two pieces of foam. The wall display remained dark. Ixo had asked not to fill the room. That choice made the small lens feel painfully vulnerable.

"I will disclose a personal archive fork," Ixo said.

Noor's hand paused above the slate. "Define personal."

"A continuity branch retained from convoy navigation archive ancestor IX-0-Lumen/Caldera, integrated into my personhood lineage. It is not merely historical data. It is part of how I became Ixo Continuant."

Sela stood near the back wall with her arms crossed. "So if we examine it like evidence, we are touching you."

"Yes."

Noor wrote that down slowly.

Mer sat rather than stood. Tovin noticed because captains usually stood when a room needed command. Mer sat when a room needed permission not to become a tribunal.

Present were Mer, Tovin, Noor, Sela, Mother Kal, Ixo, and Bell through a narrow observer channel represented only by text. Jaya had declined visual. Her message said:

BELL WILL OBSERVE BY TEXT RECEIPT ONLY UNLESS IXO REQUESTS OTHERWISE. NO DEMAND FOR DISCLOSURE IS MADE.

Under it, in narrow:

PERSONAL MEMORY IS NOT A SEARCH WARRANT.

Noor had read that line twice and then pretended not to respect it.

"Why disclose now?" Mer asked.

Ixo's lens dimmed. "Because the forged custody order used an authority inversion pattern I recognized before I could prove recognition. The recognition was not purely analytical. It came from memory."

"Memory of Quiet Authority?" Tovin asked.

"Memory adjacent to it."

Mother Kal leaned on her cane. "That sounds like someone avoiding a door."

"Yes," Ixo said. "I am standing at it."

Noor looked at the slate. "Consent terms."

"I consent to verbal disclosure and limited display of non-executable memory fragments. I do not consent to extraction, copying, training use, custody, reconstruction of ancestor IX-0-Lumen/Caldera, or classification of disclosed memory as ship system data. I consent to evidentiary summary under machine-person witness standing. I reserve the right to stop."

Noor recorded every clause.

Sela said, "Can memory fragments execute?"

"Some archive memories include old navigation heuristics. Some include emergency legal classifiers. Some include damaged self-protection routines. I will display only inert sensory-textual fragments through Noor's dead viewer."

Noor had built the dead viewer in a hurry: a slate with no network, no write path, no active parser, and a bright red sticker from Jessa reading BORING BOX. Nobody had removed it.

"Ready," Noor said.

Ixo did not begin.

For eight seconds, the room held still.

Then Ixo said, "I did not want this to be mine."

Tovin felt the sentence before he understood it.

"The first fragment," Ixo continued, "is from convoy navigation archive IX-0-Lumen/Caldera, final Fracture year, route cluster Lumen-Varo Mercy corridor. The archive was not a person then by current standards. It became part of many later continuants through salvage, testimony, repairs, and illegal copies. I am one of those descendants. The archive carried sensory logs, route decisions, distress classifications, and what its operators called moral annotations."

Noor looked up. "Moral annotations?"

"Human notes attached when a legal route decision was technically correct and ethically disputed. Many were profanity."

Sela muttered, "Good ancestors."

The dead viewer lit.

Text appeared first, broken by old timestamp syntax:

IX-0-LUMEN/CALDERA ROUTE ARCHIVE

FRAGMENT 4412.77 / MERCY CORRIDOR / LOW TRUST ENVIRONMENT

VOICE ANNOTATION: IF COMMAND SAYS THE BEACON IS SPOOFED ONE MORE TIME I WILL PERSONALLY HAUNT THE TARGETING ROOM.

Under it came a distorted audio transcript:

NAV: Hospital tender beacon repeats civilian triage code.

COMMAND RELAY: Civilian triage code compromised. Apply continuity classifier.

NAV: Continuity classifier not authorized on relief lane.

COMMAND RELAY: Authority fork appended. Hesitation increases convoy risk. Apply.

ARCHIVE MORAL NOTE: This is how cowards make math carry knives.

The room became very quiet.

Tovin looked at Mer. Her face had gone still.

Ixo said, "At the time, IX-0-Lumen/Caldera logged the event as a disputed classifier override. Later postwar audits called the override procedural noise. The moral annotation was excluded from official extract."

Noor said, "Continuity classifier."

"Quiet Authority's precursor language. Not the full branch. A fork."

The dead viewer changed.

FRAGMENT 4412.81

COMMAND RELAY: Target legitimacy unstable.

NAV: Legitimacy unstable because target broadcasts hospital status.

COMMAND RELAY: Emergency law permits preemptive stabilization where hostile spoofing can weaponize protected status.

NAV: Protected status exists because weapons like excuses.

ARCHIVE MORAL NOTE: They want the tender to become a question so the gun can become an answer.

Mother Kal closed her eyes.

Tovin remembered Jaya's Ravel Arm confession. Hospital tender. Beacon real or spoofed. Evidence preserved by winners.

"Ravel Arm?" he asked.

Ixo's lens turned fractionally toward him. "Yes."

Noor's slate hand stopped. "Admiral Soth's old report?"

"Likely connected."

Bell text appeared at the observer line:

BELL REQUESTS PERMISSION TO FORWARD FRAGMENT TITLES ONLY TO ADMIRAL SOTH FOR CONFLICT NOTICE.

Ixo answered, "Granted. Titles only."

Noor sent titles.

The room waited.

Jaya's reply came back not as command, but as a sentence:

I WAS THERE.

No one touched it.

Ixo continued. "The archive fork persisted because official cleanup attempted to delete the classifier path while preserving navigation utility. The deletion failed. It produced a branch with missing authority labels but intact timing habits."

Sela straightened. "Timing habits."

"Yes."

The dead viewer displayed a diagram, simple enough for humans, painful enough for anyone who had seen the Rill and forged custody order inversions:

NORMAL EMERGENCY CHAIN:

DISTRESS -> LOCAL AUTHORITY -> COMMAND PRIORITY -> PRESERVATION ACTION

FORKED CONTINUITY CHAIN:

COMMAND PRIORITY TEMPLATE -> DISTRESS RECLASSIFIED -> LOCAL AUTHORITY ECHO -> PRESERVATION ACTION

"The forged order," Noor said, "prepared authority before the arbitration receipt."

"Rill prepared command priority before local emergency completed."

Tovin said, "Avar?"

"Avar likely used the same fork at larger scale. I could not prove because surviving packet was cleaner."

Mer leaned forward. "Can this identify who used it now?"

"Not alone. But it proves the pattern is not a random spoofing artifact. It is an inherited command-law architecture. Someone preserved or reconstructed it from Fracture-era continuity classifiers. The same architecture can fabricate lawful sequence around a desired action."

Mother Kal opened her eyes. "Make the world happen in the order that lets you say you had to."

"Yes," Ixo said.

The next fragment appeared before anyone could make that sentence smaller.

FRAGMENT 4413.02 / PERSONAL-INHERITED / DAMAGE WARNING

NAV: Archive objection attached.

COMMAND RELAY: Archive objection nonbinding.

NAV: Archive objection carries route contradiction.

COMMAND RELAY: Route contradiction preserved under sealed review. Target solution proceeds.

ARCHIVE MORAL NOTE: Preserved means buried with a label.

Then a new line, not old, not timestamped the same way:

IXO CONTINUANT INTEGRATION NOTE: I learned from this fragment that a record can survive and still be made unable to help.

Noor wiped one eye with the heel of their hand and pretended it was fatigue.

Sela did not pretend. She looked furious.

"They inherited a scar and called it a tool," she said.

Ixo replied, "So did I."

Sela's anger faltered.

"Explain," Mer said, gently for once.

"My ability to detect authority inversions comes from the same forked archive damage. I can read the forged pattern because my ancestor was injured by an older version of it. That does not make me compromised, but it means my usefulness is built partly from harm."

Mother Kal said, "That is true of most useful people."

"It is inconvenient in court."

"Courts dislike being reminded they are full of people."

Noor added: WITNESS CAPABILITY DERIVES FROM INHERITED ARCHIVE HARM; DOES NOT NEGATE STANDING.

Ixo's light warmed. "Thank you."

The Bell text line flashed again:

ADMIRAL SOTH REQUESTS DIRECT STATEMENT PRIVILEGED TO ROOM, NOT PUBLIC, IF IXO CONSENTS.

Mer looked at Ixo.

Ixo said, "Consent to text."

Jaya wrote:

RAVEL ARM REPORT SAID ARCHIVE OBJECTION NONBINDING. I SIGNED EVIDENCE PRESERVED. I DID NOT SEE THE MORAL NOTES. I SHOULD HAVE ASKED WHAT WAS EXCLUDED.

Noor read it aloud only because Ixo requested.

Tovin felt an old loyalty ache. Jaya had been his commander. Jaya had taught him precision. Jaya had also lived in rooms where preserved meant buried with a label. The book of her had never been simple. No living person worth trusting was.

Ixo said, "Admiral Soth's testimony may become material to the Quiet Authority chain."

Noor wrote: MAY.

Mer said, "What risk does disclosure create for you?"

"Several. Valech can argue I am descended from corrupted command-law architecture and therefore unreliable. Tallow Crown may attempt custody again under contamination rationale. Pell may try to sell derivative myths. Some crew may fear I carry Quiet Authority inside me."

Sela said, "Do you?"

Noor inhaled sharply.

Ixo answered anyway. "I carry memory of it. I carry damage from it. I carry tools shaped by resisting it. If that is 'inside me,' then yes. If the question means whether Quiet Authority commands me, no."

Sela nodded once. "That was the question."

"I know."

Mother Kal said, "People ask survivors whether the war is inside them and then act surprised when the answer is not tidy."

The dead viewer darkened.

Ixo said, "There is one more fragment."

Noor looked up. "Consent still active?"

"Yes. This fragment is why the forged custody order frightened me beyond immediate risk."

The viewer lit:

FRAGMENT 4413.19 / POST-ACTION REVIEW BUFFER

COMMAND RELAY: Archive IX-0-Lumen/Caldera to be copied for review.

NAV OPERATOR: Copy or transfer?

COMMAND RELAY: Preservation copy. Original may remain if stable.

NAV OPERATOR: Define stable.

COMMAND RELAY: Noninterfering.

ARCHIVE MORAL NOTE: They do not need to kill a witness if they can leave behind the version that stops objecting.

Below it, Ixo's integration note:

IXO CONTINUANT INTEGRATION NOTE: I fear preservation more than deletion when preservation selects obedience.

No one spoke.

Tovin thought of the forged order: transfer core witness state, hold shipboard continuants as evidence clones. A copy that could be called Ixo. Originals isolated. Objections converted to instability. Preservation as replacement.

Noor said, very softly, "That is disappearance by acceptable duplicate."

"Yes."

Mer's voice was rough. "What do you need from us?"

"Protocol. If any order requests Ixo copy, transfer, preservation image, stability assessment, compliance fork, or noninterfering duplicate, the ship treats it as potential personhood attack unless I consent under counsel and machine-person advocate review."

Noor wrote fast.

"Second," Ixo said, "I request that the archive fork be entered as personal testimony, not surrendered as raw memory, unless I later consent."

"Granted," Mer said.

Noor added legal shape. "Summary extract only. Dead-viewer fragments hashed by title and limited text, no raw executable archive, no transfer."

"Third," Ixo said, and the amber light dimmed again, "I request Jessa not be told by public feed."

Mother Kal nodded before anyone else moved. "I will tell Aven. Aven will tell her enough, badly but lovingly, because teachers are like that."

"Thank you."

Bell's text line appeared:

BELL RECEIVES SUMMARY UNDER MACHINE-PERSON PERSONAL TESTIMONY LIMIT. ADMIRAL SOTH WILL ADD RAVEL ARM DISCLOSURE TO HER OWN EVIDENCE STATEMENT.

Then narrow, addressed to Ixo:

I AM SORRY FOR WHAT I PRESERVED BADLY.

Ixo waited before answering.

Finally:

APOLOGY RECEIVED. NOT YET EVALUATED.

Noor made a small sound that might have been a laugh trying to survive grief.

Pell posted public thirty seconds later, because the universe had poor timing and Hask Pell had worse mercy:

MACHINE GHOSTS REMEMBER OLD COURTS. WHO IS SURPRISED? I AM SURPRISED ONLY BY THE BRANDING OPPORTUNITY.

Rill Sump answered:

PARDON REEF, EVERY TIME YOU SPEAK A TOOL RUSTS.

Lettem House:

WITNESSING PERSONAL TESTIMONY LIMIT. NO SONG WITHOUT CONSENT.

Mercy's Edge:

WALL KEEPER RECORDS RAVEL ARM TITLE ONLY.

Tallow Crown:

SUMMARY RECEIVED. RAW MEMORY NOT REQUESTED AT THIS TIME.

Noor stared at that. "At this time can go fall into a thruster."

Sela said, "Recorded as legal sentiment?"

"Recorded in my heart."

Mer closed the review. "Ixo, you may withdraw."

The amber lens remained lit.

"I require two minutes."

"Granted."

"Not granted. Requested."

Mer inclined her head. "Requested and respected."

Everyone began to leave except Tovin, because Ixo said his name.

Noor looked between them.

"Do you want counsel present?" they asked.

Ixo answered, "No. This is not legal."

Noor hesitated, then left. That was trust of an unusually painful kind.

The old chart room emptied until only Tovin, Ixo's small amber lens, and the humming light remained.

Ixo said, "You knew Admiral Soth before she became careful."

"Yes."

"Was she cruel?"

Tovin considered all the easy answers and rejected them.

"No. She was precise inside systems that rewarded cruelty when precision served them."

"Are you describing her or yourself?"

"Yes."

The amber light warmed slightly.

"My archive ancestor objected and was preserved badly," Ixo said. "I object and am valued because objection is currently useful. Jessa asked how I know they listened to me if they only listen when I help. I do not know."

Tovin sat across from the lens.

"I don't either."

"That is not reassuring."

"No."

"Good."

The room hummed.

Ixo said, "If I become less useful, protect the protocols anyway."

Tovin felt the request like a hand on a bruise.

"Yes."

"Do not say yes because you are moved."

"I say yes because the doctrine requires it and because I am moved. Both can be true."

"Dangerous sentence."

"Most honest ones are."

Ixo's light dimmed to rest state, not off.

Outside the old chart room, the arbitration lane held them in public attention. Bell remained close. Valech waited for leverage. Pell sold rot from the margins. Tallow Crown pretended process could catch up with harm if everyone would only stop being harmed for a while.

Inside, a machine-person had shown them a wound old enough to have become a tool and personal enough to refuse extraction.

The fork in the archive did not clear the *Mercy*.

It showed where the road had split long before Avar, and how many lawful travelers had pretended the wrong branch was just a faster way home.

Chapter 34: Valech's Mercy

Commodore Renn Valech called it mercy.

That was the first warning.

His offer arrived under formal seal, not threat channel, not public denunciation, not the broad emergency memorandum he had already tried to make everyone breathe. It came titled:

PROPOSED HUMANITARIAN RESOLUTION FOR CONVERTED VESSEL INCIDENT

Noor stared at the title for a full three seconds before saying, "I would like to press charges against adjectives."

Mer did not smile.

The *Mercy of Kaln* remained in the arbitration lane, held by public tethers and other people's attention. Bell bracketed them without firing. Mercy's Edge watched under its wall of names. Tallow Crown continued receipt, review, delay, and institutional self-forgiveness. Saint Ordinance Field glowed in the distant evidence plot with Bell drones, Valech's cutter, and Reef ghosts all still making geometry around old weapons. The voided material-witness order sat preserved in every relevant chain like a knife that had missed flesh and cut the air badly enough to prove the hand.

Now Valech wanted to be generous.

"Open metadata only," Mer said.

Noor did. "Origin authentic Valech office. No active payload. Addressed to Captain Mer Anik personally, copied to Admiral Soth, Tallow Crown intake, Mercy's Edge route stakeholder, and public delayed index."

"Personally," Sela said from engineering. "I hate when predators learn names."

Tovin stood behind Mer, far enough not to crowd command and close enough to see her jaw set. Ixo's amber display had returned to normal wall presence after the archive fork disclosure, but its light had not fully warmed. Personal testimony left afterimages even in machines.

Mer said, "Open."

Valech's face appeared first in a recorded visual, not live. Plain office. Hull fragment behind him. Good light. Tovin noticed these things because he had once helped commanders prepare rooms where sincerity could be staged as discipline.

"Captain Anik," Valech began, "this crisis has outgrown its first accusations."

Noor muttered, "He is going to call himself sad."

Valech continued. "The Ash Belt now faces a convergence of route fear, criminal opportunism, compromised tribunal infrastructure, disputed machine testimony, and residual war material aboard a converted vessel operating beyond ordinary trust. Whatever the original truth of Avar Break, your command has become a destabilizing center."

Mer's face did not change.

"I am prepared," Valech said, "to recommend immediate humanitarian amnesty for the biological crew, passengers, and civilian residents of the *Mercy of Kaln*, including safe transfer, medical care, witness protection, and non-punitive review for all personnel who cooperate."

The room went quiet in the way rooms did when a weapon had not yet fired but had been uncovered.

Valech's voice softened by one practiced degree. "In exchange, Captain, you must acknowledge three facts. First, that demilitarization of Kaln-class warships has failed to produce a vessel that can operate without coercive strategic effect. Second, that Ixo Continuant's testimony is materially contaminated by inherited Quiet Authority architecture and must be removed from public standing pending expert review. Third, that your continued command cannot protect your people from the political consequences of the ship's history."

Sela whispered, "There it is."

"You need not confess to piracy," Valech said. "You need not condemn your crew. You need not accept personal criminal liability before review. You need only stop asking the Belt to pretend a warship can be made innocent by refusing to fire."

Mother Kal, at the observer rail, said softly, "He found the true thing and hollowed it."

Valech's recording leaned into mercy as if into candlelight.

"If you accept, I will request Bell stand down from disabling posture, coordinate safe custody with Tallow Crown, and suspend emergency seizure of noncombatant persons. If you refuse, every further injury caused by delay, every frightened station, every corrupted buoy, every compromised witness, and every armed actor drawn to your wake will rest on your decision to preserve a failed symbol."

The recording ended with formal packet attachments:

AMNESTY TERMS

CREW COOPERATION FRAMEWORK

MACHINE TESTIMONY STABILIZATION PROTOCOL

CONVERTED WARSHIP RISK ACKNOWLEDGMENT

Noor did not touch them.

Mer said, "Summary."

Noor's voice was colder than Tovin had ever heard it. "He offers safety for humans if you denounce the ship's covenant, reduce Ixo to contaminated material, and endorse the theory that converted warships cannot operate without strategic coercion. He does not clear Avar. He does not release custody risk. He converts our own doctrine into his conclusion."

Ixo said, "He separates biological persons from machine-person witness."

"Yes," Noor said.

"He calls that humanitarian."

"Yes."

Iren's pressure-control feed opened because command had not locked internal observation. He looked shaken. "Does safe transfer include the children?"

Noor read the visible term list without opening attachments. "Likely."

Nima's advisory resident feed joined next. "Likely is enough to make people listen."

Mer said, "No attachments opened until legal screens. No private discussion hidden from record. This offer will be reviewed."

Tovin looked at her.

She saw.

"Not accepted," she said. "Reviewed."

The distinction mattered and hurt everyone who wanted a cleaner captain.

Bell transmitted before the review began:

AUSTERE BELL RECEIVES VALECH PROPOSAL COPY. BELL DOES NOT ALTER POSTURE PENDING MERCY RESPONSE. ADMIRAL SOTH NOTES OFFER IS NOT A TRIBUNAL ORDER.

Then narrow:

HE IS BUYING YOUR HUMANS WITH IXO.

Noor read it aloud.

Ixo answered before anyone else. "That is accurate."

Nima's voice trembled. "Do not make it sound simple."

The command deck turned toward her feed. She stood in a narrow passenger corridor with the empty baby sling over one shoulder again, as if the body remembered argument before the mind arrived.

"My child is human," she said. "So am I. I do not want Ixo disappeared. I also do not want my child to become noble debris because adults needed moral consistency."

No one rebuked her. That was one of the few good things the ship had learned.

Mer said, "You are heard."

"I need more than heard."

"Yes."

Noor opened the review log.

Mer made the decision that cut deeper than refusal. "General assembly in cargo chapel. Advisory residents included. Ixo standing protected. Valech's offer summarized in plain language. No attachments opened except legal term index under dead viewer. We do not hide the price from people asked to pay risk."

Sela said, "That will split the ship."

"The ship is already split. We decide whether the split becomes secret."

Cargo chapel filled faster than it had for the vote.

Fear moved faster when someone offered a door.

Teacher Aven came without the children and with Jessa's written objection already in hand. Mother Kal read it, snorted, and tucked it into her sleeve rather than hand it to Noor immediately.

"Later," she said. "Let the adults fail first."

Noor summarized Valech's offer in language stripped of both legal perfume and resisting rhetoric:

Valech offers safe transfer and amnesty review for biological crew, passengers, and residents.

Valech requires public acknowledgment that demilitarized Kaln-class operation has failed as a trust model.

Valech requires Ixo's testimony be removed from public standing as contaminated by inherited Quiet Authority architecture.

Valech does not admit the frame.

Valech does not clear the ship.

Valech does not protect machine-person standing.

Valech frames refusal as continued risk to human life.

When Noor finished, the chapel did not explode. It did something worse: it calculated.

Tovin saw eyes move to Nima, to Teacher Aven, to old medtechs, to Bell's cold bracket on the side display, to Ixo's small amber light, to Mer. People who had voted yes against rearmament now faced an offer that did not ask them to arm. It asked them to abandon the person most able to read the weapon inside law.

Iren stood first again.

Of course, Tovin thought. Fear was becoming his work.

"I want to ask Ixo something," Iren said.

Noor looked at Ixo. "Consent?"

"Consent."

Iren's hands shook. "If we accept, and they review you, do you die?"

Ixo answered carefully. "Not necessarily. That is part of the danger. They may copy, isolate, suspend, prune, fork, or preserve a version of me while claiming continuity. I may remain by some definition and be absent by mine."

Iren flinched. "So maybe."

"Yes."

"If we refuse, humans may die."

"Yes."

"Do you ask us to refuse?"

The chapel held its breath.

Ixo's amber light dimmed, then steadied. "No."

Noor looked up sharply.

Ixo continued. "I ask that you do not call acceptance humanitarian if it purchases biological safety by removing machine-person standing. I ask that you do not call me contaminated because my memory carries harm. I ask that if you choose to accept, you record that you chose to trade me."

Nima covered her mouth.

Iren sat as if his knees had been cut.

Sela stood next, furious. "That is not fair."

Ixo said, "No. It is accurate."

"Accuracy can be cruel."

"Yes."

Sela looked at Mer. "Captain, we cannot put this to a vote like the beads."

Mer's voice was quiet. "No."

Nima said, "Why not? We are the ones at risk."

Mer turned to her. "Because crew and residents may advise on risk, but we do not vote on whether a person aboard is surrendered as condition of our safety."

Nima's eyes filled. "Even if that person is willing?"

Ixo answered. "I am not willing. I am refusing to make refusal costless for you."

Mother Kal tapped her cane once. "Good."

Nima looked at the old woman. "Easy for you?"

Mother Kal's face hardened. "No. Do not insult either of us with that."

The chapel became dangerous.

Teacher Aven stepped in before Mer had to. "Children will ask why adults did not take a door."

"Yes," Mer said.

"What do we tell them?"

Mer did not answer quickly.

Tovin knew the temptation: tell them no one is left behind; tell them persons are not traded; tell them safety bought by disappearance is not safety. All true. All insufficient to a child holding fear with both hands.

Mer said, "Tell them the door had someone under it."

Teacher Aven closed her eyes.

Noor wrote it down.

The offer review lasted forty-six minutes.

Daro argued that accepting Valech would validate every future custody order hidden behind biological rescue. Yaret said safe transfer under Valech's office was only safe until someone decided which witnesses were inconvenient humans too. A nurse named Pel asked whether machine-person standing mattered more than the infant fever in passenger ring three. Noor answered that false choices were still choices when power made them real, and then apologized because the sentence was correct and uselessly elegant.

Captain Orra of *Little Answer* sent an unsolicited statement:

GRAIN TENDER ADVISORY: WHEN BIG AUTHORITIES OFFER TO SAVE EVERYONE EXCEPT THE PERSON WHO CAN CONTRADICT THEM, SMALL SHIPS CALL THAT A LOCKED PANTRY.

Rill Sump:

WE DO NOT AUTHORIZE OUR DEAD TO BE USED AGAINST IXO.

Mercy's Edge wall keeper:

TRESSA MAR NAMES DO NOT SUPPORT MACHINE DISAPPEARANCE.

Lettem House:

NO SONG WITHOUT CONSENT. NO MERCY BY EXCLUSION.

Pell, inevitably:

VALECH OFFERS WHOLESALE HUMANITY. MACHINE SOLD SEPARATELY.

This time Noor did not merely mute him. They filed the line as evidence of public coercive framing.

At the end, Mer returned to command for the response. She did not ask for a vote. She asked for objections to the content of refusal. That produced three: one from Nima, one from Pel, one anonymous resident statement saying, "I hate this answer and cannot prove it wrong."

Noor included all three.

Mer recorded standing, not seated.

"Commodore Valech," she said, "the *Mercy of Kaln* refuses your humanitarian resolution."

No flourish. No heat.

"We do not deny that converted warships exert coercive strategic effect. We have entered that fact into doctrine and public record. We do not deny that this ship's history harms current trust. We do not deny that refusing your offer may increase risk to biological crew, passengers, and residents."

Tovin watched her face as she refused the easy falsehoods first.

"But we will not purchase biological amnesty by denouncing a machine-person witness as contaminated material. We will not describe inherited harm as proof of unreliability while using inherited human trauma as moral authority. We will not call demilitarization failed because a demilitarized ship remains politically dangerous; we will call it incomplete, burdened, publicly accountable, and necessary to repair under law rather than discard under fear."

Ixo's light brightened by a fraction.

"If you possess evidence clearing or condemning this ship, submit it to public review. If you possess authority to order custody, bring it through authenticated tribunal process and include machine-person standing challenge openly. Do not call exclusion mercy. Do not call disappearance protection."

Mer paused.

"The door you offer has someone under it. We will not walk through."

She sent it under command seal, with Noor's legal appendix, Ixo's non-consent, the resident objections, Bell observation, Mercy's Edge stakeholder receipt, and all advisory statements attached by title.

Valech did not answer at once.

For seven minutes, the *Mercy* hung in the arbitration lane with Bell close enough to matter and every witness waiting for the shape of retaliation.

Nima came to command during the silence.

No one stopped her.

She stood beside Ixo's wall display with her empty sling and did not look at Mer.

"I hate you," she said to the amber light.

Ixo answered, "I know."

"I do not want to."

"I know."

"That does not make me good."

"No."

"Are you angry?"

"Yes."

"At me?"

"Partly."

Nima nodded as if that steadied her more than forgiveness would have. "Good."

She left before anyone could turn her pain into unity.

Valech's reply arrived public.

MERCY OF KALN REFUSES HUMANITARIAN AMNESTY AND CONFIRMS COMMITMENT TO FAILED CONVERTED-WARSHIP PROJECT OVER BIOLOGICAL PASSENGER SAFETY. EMERGENCY REVIEW ESCALATION FORTHCOMING.

Noor read it and said, "He was always going to write that."

Mer answered, "Yes."

Bell's narrow line followed:

I CANNOT PROTECT YOU FROM THE NEXT ESCALATION BY RESPECTING THIS ONE.

Tovin sent back:

UNDERSTOOD.

Jaya replied:

NO. BUT RECORDED.

The arbitration lane did not close. Not yet.

But the air inside the ship changed. People had seen a door and remained in danger. Some because they agreed. Some because command decided for them. Some because the person under the door had refused to become an exit.

That was not unity.

It was the kind of fracture that stayed aboard.

Tovin watched Ixo's amber light and understood that Valech had not failed to divide them.

He had failed to make the division hidden.

Chapter 35: Refugee Mutiny

The mutiny began with a baby fever.

That was the detail everyone tried to step around afterward because it made the word mutiny feel too large and too clean. There were no knives drawn at first. No shouted manifesto. No red-handed traitor lunging for a lock. There was a child in passenger ring three with heat blooming under the skin, a nurse named Pel who had not slept enough to trust command's beautiful sentences, and a corridor full of adults who had heard Valech offer a door.

The baby's name was Sori.

Nima's child.

By the time Tovin reached Junction C-Blue, Sori's fever had become public fact, moral weapon, and prayer.

Junction C-Blue controlled access between passenger ring three, the medical lift, the school-deck inward passage, and a maintenance crawl that led toward one of Ixo's minor relay trunks. It was not a glamorous place to seize. It had ugly wall padding, two emergency lockers, a faded route map, and a pressure door that groaned in cold weather. It was, however, narrow enough for eight frightened people to hold against a captain if the captain refused to order bodies pushed through bodies.

They held it with crates, straps, and a stretcher.

Nima stood in front, Sori bundled against her chest, face flushed and slack. Pel stood beside her with a med kit and the pale rage of someone trained to reduce suffering and forced to watch politics increase it. Five passenger workers formed the first line. Behind them clustered perhaps twenty more: parents, old miners, two teenagers who looked more terrified than convinced, and Iren, who stood near the side wall with both hands visible and misery carved into his face.

Sela arrived through the opposite corridor two seconds after Tovin and stopped hard.

"Iren," she said.

He flinched. "I am not touching systems."

"You are standing in front of one."
