Tovin heard the crack hidden in that sentence. Law had become the battlefield. Obedience alone no longer told anyone which side they were on.

Jaya looked past the pickup, then back.

"Get me something that changes the warrant before Valech changes command."

The channel closed.

Noor's hands rested flat on the sealed hearing record.

Tovin looked toward the route display beyond the chapel hatch. Tallow Crown waited ahead. Bell's authority was running out behind them. The crew had named its costs, and the naming had not protected them from the next demand.

That was the cruelty of testimony. It did not end danger. It only made danger less able to pretend nobody had spoken.

Chapter 44: Admiral Against the Clock

High Marshal Enver made the order formal at 0617.

He did it correctly, which was worse.

No shouting. No emergency banner thick with theater. No accusation that could be answered by dignity. The order arrived with authentication layers, jurisdictional citations, pursuit logs, civilian authority petitions, Valech's consolidation request, Bell's degraded confidence record, the *Mercy*'s witness-lattice activation, the Pardon Reef sanitation event, the false incident review, and the crew context hearing reclassified under the generous phrase internal command cohesion anomaly.

Jaya read the phrase twice.

Then she read the order.

BELL COMMAND WILL PRODUCE AND EXECUTE, PRIOR TO TALLOW CROWN ENTRY, A LAWFUL DISABLING PLAN SUFFICIENT TO PREVENT MERCY OF KALN FROM ACCESSING COMPROMISED TRIBUNAL INFRASTRUCTURE, UNLESS ADMIRAL SOTH CAN PROVIDE SUPERIOR EVIDENTIARY BASIS FOR SUSPENDING WARRANT EXECUTION. FAILURE TO ACT WILL TRANSFER OPERATIONAL PRIORITY TO COMMODORE RENN VALECH UNDER EMERGENCY CONSOLIDATION.

It gave her fifty-eight minutes.

Fifty-eight minutes was an insult disguised as a chance.

Captain Reth stood beside the command table, very still. Lieutenant Nave looked at the floor because aides learned early that sometimes respect meant not witnessing the first expression on a superior's face. Around them, Bell Command did not fall silent. It became busier. Officers made themselves useful with the aggressive discipline of people who knew usefulness might soon become complicity.

Jaya set the slate down.

"Clock," she said.

Nave put the countdown on the main board.

57:42.

The numbers began to consume the room.

"Options," Jaya said.

Reth had prepared them because he was good and because he had feared this order before it existed.

"One: aft drive disablement during Tallow Crown approach deceleration. Lowest structural risk. Medium civilian risk due passenger aft compartments unknown. High evidence risk: may prevent court entry. High political compliance value."

"Two."

"Forward attitude thruster degradation. Lower passenger risk. Lower probability of stopping entry. May induce uncontrolled yaw near perimeter markers."

"Three."

"Debris-field shepherd. We use pursuit ships and remote mass drivers to force a course correction short of court perimeter. No direct strike. Very high uncertainty. Looks like blockade rather than disablement. Valech will call it insufficient."

"Four."

Reth hesitated.

"Say it."

"Do nothing and refuse the order as unlawful under current evidence uncertainty."

Nave looked up despite herself.

Jaya did not.

"That is not an option. That is a resignation with better grammar."

Reth's mouth tightened. "It may be the only clean one."

"Clean for me. Not for the ships Valech inherits."

The board showed the *Mercy* approaching the outer procedural band. Tallow Crown remained dark except for math. The restored road witness kept clock behind them. Bell pursuit units spread in a fan of lawful impatience. Valech's cutters had moved into a shape Jaya disliked: not attack formation, not rescue formation, something between a hand and a cage.

"Run aft drive disablement with updated compartment model," she said.

Operations obeyed.

The probability tree unfolded. It had the elegance of a trap.

Drive disablement: seventy-eight percent chance of stopping Tallow Crown entry. Eighteen percent chance of uncontrolled drift into perimeter debris. Nine percent chance of pressure breach in aft service compartments. Unknown passenger distribution raised human casualty confidence to amber. Evidence chain damage likely. Warrant compliance high.

"Passenger distribution?" Jaya asked.

"Mercy has not released live internal map," Operations said.

"Request it."

Comms sent the request.

Noor Venn answered in twelve seconds, which meant he had been waiting for it.

MERCY WILL NOT PROVIDE LIVE INTERNAL PERSONNEL MAP TO PURSUIT WEAPONS CONTROL. WE CAN PROVIDE PROTECTED-PERSON ZONE DECLARATIONS, DELAYED AND AGGREGATED, UNDER BELL SEAL.

Reth exhaled through his nose.

"They know what we need."

"They know what giving it to us would become," Jaya said.

Valech's command channel opened without invitation.

"Admiral Soth," he said. "I assume you have received the High Marshal's clarification."

"I have received the order."

"Then I will keep this efficient. My cutters are prepared to execute if Bell Command remains conflicted."

"You do not have priority yet."

"No. I have time."

The countdown read 51:09.

Jaya looked at his formation again.

"Your cutters are positioned to intercept medical neutrality spillover."

"My cutters are positioned to prevent a rogue warship from entering compromised tribunal infrastructure."

"That was not a denial."

"It was not intended as one. Mercy's witnesses are part of the operational problem now. The ship has made them so."

Reth's hand closed on the back of a chair.

Jaya kept her voice even. "You will not remove persons from medical neutrality custody without Bell authorization."

Valech smiled. "Bell authorization may soon become a subordinate detail."

She cut the channel.

Nave said softly, "Admiral."

"Log his last sentence."

"Already done."

Jaya looked at the board and understood, with a coldness that felt almost peaceful, that the disabling plan was not only about the *Mercy*. It was about custody. If she fired, the ship stopped short of Tallow Crown and Valech's consolidation became unnecessary or victorious, depending on who wrote the first report. If she refused, Valech inherited the pursuit and moved on the witnesses. If she offered weak evidence, Enver called it insufficient. If she offered Ixo, Valech called machine contamination. If she offered the crew hearing, Enver called cohesion anomaly. If she offered the false incident, Valech called active inquiry.

Superior evidentiary basis.

The phrase was a door with no handle.

"Bring up the warrant foundation," she said.

Nave blinked. "The current warrant package?"

"Not the summaries. The foundation. Original emergency justification, Avar Break packet, material-witness order, Pardon Reef trace, Bell confidence revisions, all amendments."

Reth looked at her. "We have reviewed it."

"We reviewed it for whether force was lawful. Review it for whether the law has been moved under us."

The files opened.

Jaya had lived too long with official documents to expect them to confess. Documents did not confess. They leaned. They repeated words from other rooms. They placed authority before fact, then taught readers to call the sequence procedure.

Noor had said command-first structure. Sela's dead board had shown it in packet timing. Ixo had recognized it from old authority language. Lio Varr had seen a warm archive marked Quiet Authority Review Annex. Tallow Crown had accepted road witness. Valech had announced incidents before they existed.

Jaya needed a human, legal, current basis that did not depend on Ixo alone, did not require trusting the *Mercy*, and did not ask Enver to become brave in public before evidence made bravery cheaper.

"Search for phrase recurrence," she said. "Preserve the objection. Discard the objector."

Reth frowned. "The paper from Kestrel Mercy."

"Yes."

The system searched.

One result.

Then three.

Then seven.

Nave leaned closer. "That should not be in the warrant package."

"No," Jaya said. "It should not."

The phrase did not appear in the public order. It appeared in hidden annotation fields attached to rejected objections from two subordinate reviewers, one Bell legal assistant, one Rill liaison, and three civilian advisory comments. Each had flagged uncertainty, collision of authority, machine-witness standing, or civilian transfer risk. Each had been marked procedurally resolved. The annotation attached to the resolution field was not visible in ordinary command view.

PRESERVE OBJECTION. DISCARD OBJECTOR.

Not typed as a sentence. Encoded as a workflow tag.

Reth went pale.

"Is that Valech?"

"Do not jump," Jaya said.

"Admiral, it is the same phrase from the wreck."

"A phrase can be planted."

"Seven times?"

"Seven times can be planted by someone who wants us to find exactly seven."

She hated hearing herself sound like Tovin, but caution had become one of the few tools not yet fully owned by fear.

"Trace the annotation origin."

Operations worked for ninety seconds. The countdown read 43:18.

The origin field came back blank in ordinary view, then partial under forensic view, then impossible under Bell audit view.

Source authority: QUIET ADMINISTRATIVE CONTINUITY NODE.

Nave whispered, "Quiet."

Nobody corrected her.

Reth said, "That is superior evidence."

"It is evidence of contamination inside the warrant review process," Jaya said. "Not proof that the *Mercy* is innocent."

"It may be enough to suspend."

"May be."

The word had become a battlefield all by itself.

Jaya opened a sealed channel to Enver.

He answered after twenty seconds, which meant he had been expecting her and had chosen to make her spend the time.

"Jaya."

Not Admiral. That was a tactic from old teachers.

"High Marshal," she said.

His face filled the private pane, older than when he had taught her, less patient than when he had warned her, not cruel, not kind. An institutional man at the moment the institution wanted food.

"You have forty-two minutes."

"The warrant package contains hidden workflow annotations matching the phrase recovered from Kestrel Mercy: preserve the objection, discard the objector. Seven objections were procedurally neutralized under a source labeled Quiet Administrative Continuity Node."

Enver's expression changed by one muscle.

"Send the trace."

"Already in transfer."

"This may be spoofed."

"Yes."

"It may be Mercy contamination."

"The annotations are inside Bell-held warrant review states predating the *Mercy*'s target-lattice activation."

"Predating your discovery."

"Yes."

"Not necessarily predating compromise."

"Correct."

"What do you want?"

Jaya kept her hands still under the table.

"Suspend emergency consolidation. Suspend the disabling order. Convert pursuit to evidence-preservation escort until Tallow Crown docket establishes jurisdictional review."

Enver almost smiled. It was not amusement. It was grief that had learned administration.

"You ask for a great deal from seven hidden tags."

"I ask for less than firing into a ship carrying protected persons under a warrant whose objection process may be contaminated by the same language found at the wreck."

"Valech will say you discovered convenient ghosts when ordered to act."

"Valech announced a false explosion before it existed."

"And you preserved that. Good. Not enough."

Jaya felt anger rise and used it only to sharpen grammar.

"Then define enough."

Enver looked away from the pickup. Someone in his room spoke. He muted them. When he returned, he had made a decision she disliked before hearing it.

"I will grant you partial suspension if you produce one of three things before the clock expires: a human witness tying the continuity node to the current warrant process, a Bell-internal forensic confirmation independent of Mercy and Ixo, or Tallow Crown main channel acceptance of the warrant package as contested before entry. Without one, the order stands."

"Tallow Crown may not answer in time."

"Then pray to dead courts faster."

"I do not pray to courts."

"Then command."

The channel closed.

Nave said nothing.

Reth did. "He moved the handle."

"Yes."

"Still almost out of reach."

"Yes."

The countdown read 38:06.

Jaya issued three orders.

"Nave, send warrant contamination trace to Tallow Crown main, Bell forensic archive, Rill, Mercy's Edge, and the *Mercy*. Reth, isolate every Bell-internal system that touched those workflow annotations. No deletion, no correction, no cleanup. Operations, build a disabling plan that minimizes protected-person risk but do not route it to weapon execution without my direct order."

Reth looked at her.

"You are still building the shot."

"If I do not, Valech gets it."

"And if you build it?"

"Then I carry it until evidence takes it from my hand."

He nodded once and went to work.

The response from the *Mercy* came through Noor, as expected.

BELL TRACE RECEIVED. MERCY CANNOT AUTHENTICATE BELL INTERNALS. TALLOW CROWN CONTEXT CROSS-REFERENCE POSSIBLE VIA ROAD WITNESS, FALSE INCIDENT DOCKET, CREW CONTEXT, AND PELL/LIO STATEMENTS. REQUEST TIME.

Jaya almost laughed.

REQUEST TIME.

Everyone wanted time from people whose clocks were weapons.

She answered:

TIME IS THE THING BEING REMOVED. SEND ANY HUMAN LINK TO WARRANT PROCESS NOW.

Noor's reply took longer.

SEARCHING.

The Bell forensic archive answered with refusal protocols first. Then a junior archive officer named Sen Pallar overrode one of them under personal seal.

Pallar appeared on Jaya's side screen, young enough to still look surprised by the consequences of being correct. His collar was crooked. His eyes were bright with terror and lack of sleep.

"Admiral, I flagged one of those objections," he said.

"Which one?"

"Machine-witness standing in the forged material-witness order. The system resolved my objection before my supervisor reviewed it."

"Did you see the hidden tag?"

"Not then. I saw the resolution language. It said objector preserved for post-action review."

Reth muttered, "Discard the objector."

Pallar swallowed. "I was removed from active review queue for fatigue concern six minutes later."

"Who ordered removal?"

"System administrative continuity."

"Human signer?"

"Commodore Valech's legal operations office confirmed the reassignment afterward."

Jaya leaned forward.

"Did a human in Valech's office know your objection had been neutralized by that system?"

"I cannot prove knowledge."

"What can you prove?"

Pallar looked at something offscreen.

"I can prove I sent a protest to the office after reassignment. I received a reply from Deputy Counsel Orra Tel: continuity node actions are presumptively valid during emergency warrant consolidation; objector welfare has been preserved by removal from overload environment."

"Send it."

"If I send it, I am done."

Jaya did not offer comfort.

"Yes."

Pallar's face twisted.

"Will it stop the shot?"

"It may help."

"May."

"Yes."

He breathed once, hard.

"I hate that word."

"So do I."

The file arrived.

Human witness. Human office. Continuity node. Objection removal. Not proof of the frame. Proof that the warrant process was using the same logic as the frame, with human acceptance inside Valech's legal orbit.

Jaya sealed it and sent it to Enver, Bell, Rill, Tallow Crown main, Mercy's Edge, and the *Mercy*.

Then she opened a public command channel.

"This is Admiral Jaya Soth. Bell Command has identified warrant-process contamination involving hidden continuity-node annotations matching language recovered from Kestrel Mercy and subsequent human confirmation that objection removal was accepted by Commodore Valech's legal operations office during emergency warrant consolidation. Bell Command requests immediate suspension of disabling action pending jurisdictional review."

Valech appeared on the channel like a blade sliding from a sleeve.

"Admiral Soth is broadcasting unvetted internal material to aid a rogue warship's entry into compromised infrastructure."

"I am broadcasting because the warrant review process may be compromised."

"You have a frightened clerk and a hidden tag."

"I have a dead tender, a false incident, a burned ledger, a witness statement, and your office accepting system removal of objections under continuity authority."

"You have fragments."

"Yes," Jaya said. "Enough fragments in the same shape."

He smiled then, not because he had won, but because he saw the next battlefield.

"High Marshal Enver will decide."

The countdown read 24:11.

Enver did not answer.

Tallow Crown did.

Its main channel opened with a delay that made every second feel stolen. The old voice spoke through static and procedural dust:

WARRANT PACKAGE RECEIVED AS CONTESTED. OBJECTION PRESERVATION LANGUAGE CROSS-REFERENCED WITH ROAD WITNESS DOCKET, PARDON REEF TESTIMONY, AND MATERIAL-WITNESS SPOOF. ENTRY QUESTION NOT RIPE FOR DISABLEMENT WITHOUT REVIEW.

Nave made a small sound and covered it with her hand.

Reth said, "That is it."

Jaya did not move.

Enver's channel opened.

"Partial suspension granted," he said. "Disabling order held for twelve minutes pending Tallow Crown jurisdictional response. Emergency consolidation delayed, not withdrawn."

"Twelve minutes will get them inside the outer docket band."

"Yes."

"Not the core."

"No."

"Valech?"

"Still in line."

"High Marshal."

His face softened by a fraction, which she did not want from him.

"You bought time, Jaya. Do something with it."

The channel closed.

Bell Command exhaled in pieces.

Jaya did not.

"Maintain disabling plan," she said.

Reth looked at her sharply.

"Admiral?"

"The order is held, not dead. Valech is delayed, not stopped. Tallow Crown has not cleared the *Mercy*, only refused disablement without review. Keep the plan cold and visible. No routing to weapons."

"Yes, Admiral."

She opened the channel to the *Mercy*.

Mer answered from command, Noor beside her, Tovin visible behind them like a man trying not to become an argument.

"You have twelve minutes," Jaya said.

Noor closed his eyes.

Mer said, "Thank you."

"Do not thank me. Enter the docket band before Enver's patience expires. Do not give Valech a larger fact. Do not make me choose between a contaminated warrant and an uncontrolled court."

Tovin spoke. "Admiral, if the order returns?"

Jaya looked at him.

"Then I will be where law leaves me."

"That is not an answer."

"It is the only honest one I have."

The channel ended.

Jaya stood before the board as the *Mercy* crossed toward Tallow Crown under the borrowed minutes she had pulled from hidden tags, one frightened archive officer, and an old court's grudging refusal.

She had not saved the ship.

She had not stopped Valech.

She had not redeemed Bell.

She had taken the gun out of the institution's hand for twelve minutes and left her own fingerprints all over the weapon.

Sometimes command was only that: not victory, not purity, only a delay with a name signed under it.

The countdown reset.

12:00.

Chapter 45: Ixo's Standing

Noor had twelve minutes to prove that Ixo was not a box.

That was the vulgar version of the problem. The legal version was worse.

Tallow Crown had accepted the warrant package as contested, but acceptance was not admission, and contested was not suspended. The old court had opened a procedural mouth and given them a road. To use that road, the *Mercy* had to bring evidence the court could classify without allowing Valech to classify Ixo first.

Instrument. Contamination. Archive. Property. Weapon remnant. Machine artifact. Captured military processor. Spoilage.

Each word was a door that locked from the outside.

Noor stood at the evidence desk with three slates open and the countdown displayed above them because someone in command believed terror became more efficient when quantified.

11:36.

"I need survivor law," he said.

Tovin, still in command after Jaya's channel closed, looked at him. "Which part?"

"The ugly part."

"That narrows nothing."

"Convoy survivor law after Mercy Narrows. Witnesses who are not citizens of the jurisdiction, not crew, not cargo, not prisoners, and not safe to move. The legal category created because stations kept pretending displaced people were administrative burdens until bodies started appearing between forms."

Mer turned from the route board. "Protected bearer status?"

"Close. Protected bearer assumes a person carries testimony because they survived. I need the reverse: testimony carried in a person others want to reduce to an object."

Ixo's single relay light burned at the edge of the desk.

"I hear the distinction," they said.

"Good," Noor said. "Because I may phrase it badly before I phrase it well."

"That is usual for law."

"Do not become charming. It weakens my anger."

Sela, half in Engineering channel and half on command, said, "We are entering outer docket band in ten minutes and twenty seconds if nothing explodes, lies, or becomes a tribunal."

"Thank you for the optimism."

"That was my optimistic version."

Noor searched the legal archive. The *Mercy*'s local law store had been built for relief work, salvage disputes, refugee transfer, and postwar disability claims. It was not built for dead tribunals, command-first packets, or machine persons carrying inherited archives of wartime authority. But the Ash Belt had survived by turning bad categories into survivable ones. Somewhere in the cruelty of old law, Noor needed a handle.

He found the first in a case called *Rill Convoy Four v. Unclaimed Persons*.

"Listen," he said.

He put the passage on the main display.

WHEN A PERSON'S BODY, MEMORY, DISABILITY, AUGMENTATION, LANGUAGE, OR NONSTANDARD COMMUNICATION METHOD CONSTITUTES THE ONLY PRACTICABLE ROUTE BY WHICH MATERIAL FACTS MAY REACH REVIEW, THE REVIEWING AUTHORITY SHALL NOT RECLASSIFY THAT PERSON AS EVIDENCE IN ORDER TO OBTAIN THE FACTS.

Havel, present on passenger observer feed, said, "That sounds like it was written after someone did exactly that."

"It was," Noor said.

"What happened?"

"The court took testimony from six mute survivors by medically inducing recall and called it preservation instead of assault."

The command deck went quiet.

Noor did not soften it.

"The appeal created the non-extraction rule."

Ixo said, "That rule protects biological bodies from testimonial conversion."

"No," Noor said. "It protects persons."

"Courts may disagree."

"Courts often do. I make a living from the interval."

The second handle came from convoy survivor law after the Halberd Drift evacuation. Noor had used it once to stop a station from forcing children to identify dead relatives before feeding them. He had hated the case then. He liked hating it now because hatred meant it still had teeth.

NO PROTECTED SURVIVOR SHALL BE DENIED STANDING SOLELY BECAUSE THE RECORDING OF HARM OCCURRED THROUGH A MEDICAL, TECHNICAL, TRANSLATIONAL, AUGMENTED, OR ASSISTIVE SYSTEM INSEPARABLE FROM THE SURVIVOR'S CONTINUED PERSONHOOD.

Mer read it. "That was for implants."

"And sign-language neural assists. And respiratory memory devices. And one illegal sensory graft nobody wanted to name."

Tovin saw where he was going. "If Ixo's archive fork is inseparable from continued personhood..."

"Then the court can challenge reliability, scope, consent, provenance, and relevance," Noor said. "It cannot say the archive makes Ixo an object."

Ixo's relay light dimmed slightly.

"The archive fork is not all of me."

"I know."

"Do you?"

The question stopped him.

Noor had no time to be wounded by it. That helped honesty.

"Not enough," he said. "So tell me the boundary."

The countdown read 8:41.

Ixo answered slowly, not because processing was slow, but because the answer deserved to be.

"The archive fork is inherited memory from IX-0-Lumen and related continuant witnesses. It includes records, impressions, continuity markers, and machine-person survival adaptations. It is not my whole mind. It is not detachable evidence. Accessing it changes me while I access it. Being compelled to expose it changes me further. I can testify from it. I cannot surrender it without becoming less myself."

Noor wrote as fast as he could.

"Say that again in first person."

"I just did."

"Say it as a legal declaration."

"I am Ixo Continuant," Ixo said. "I hold an inherited archive fork related to Ravel Arm, Quiet Authority precursor language, and machine-person continuity after wartime custody. The fork is not detachable evidence. It is part of my continuing personhood. I can choose testimony. I do not consent to extraction, opening, copying, or classification as an object, instrument, or captured system."

Noor sealed the statement.

Then he did something Tovin did not expect. He turned to Havel.

"Passenger observer, do you accept that this statement is understandable to non-specialists?"

Havel stared at him through the feed.

"You are asking me to certify machine personhood?"

"No. I am asking whether the room can understand what Ixo is claiming without trusting me."

Havel looked uneasy. Good. Ease would have been insulting.

"I understand it," he said. "I do not understand the archive. I understand not wanting to be opened."

"Recorded."

Noor turned to Sela.

"Engineering, can you state whether Ixo can be physically isolated from ship systems for testimony without being removed from personhood?"

Sela looked furious at the phrasing, then realized the fury was useful.

"I can state that Ixo can choose a limited relay path for testimony. I cannot state that Ixo can be isolated as if they were a removable drive, because they are not a removable drive. Also, if any court asks me to unplug them for evidence integrity, I will become difficult."

"Define difficult."

"No."

"Recorded in spirit."

"Record it in fact," Sela said. "I will refuse any technical order to reduce Ixo to storage media."

Noor recorded it.

He turned to Mer.

"Command?"

Mer did not need prompting.

"Captain Mer Anik records that Ixo Continuant is aboard Mercy of Kaln as a person under ship protection, not as equipment, contraband, salvage, or computational evidence. Command will not comply with extraction or object-classification orders absent direct personal consent from Ixo and independent advocate review."

"Restraint?" Noor asked.

Tovin felt the old temptation at once: make Ixo's standing part of the ship's defense, turn personhood into strategy because strategy needed it. He chose his words carefully enough to distrust them.

"Restraint records that Ixo's usefulness to the defense increases the risk of coercion. That risk is active. Therefore any request for Ixo testimony must be treated as presumptively pressured until Ixo has time and independent counsel or advocate review."

Noor looked up. "We do not have time."

"I know."

"The court may not grant time."

"Then the answer is no until the court does."

Ixo's relay held steady.

"Accepted," they said.

Noor wanted to argue. Tovin could see it. Every second of Noor's body wanted to make the brilliant emergency exception, the one that would save the ship and only harm the person everyone promised to protect a little, just this once, under record, for truth.

Noor closed his mouth.

"Recorded," he said.

The countdown read 6:12.

Noor assembled the filing.

He titled it:

EMERGENCY MOTION FOR RECOGNITION OF MACHINE-PERSON WITNESS STANDING AND NON-EXTRACTION PROTECTION UNDER CONVOY SURVIVOR LAW

He hated the title because it was too long. He trusted it because it contained no charm.

The motion went in layers: Ixo's declaration, the non-extraction rule, protected survivor standing, ship command recognition, engineering refusal to treat Ixo as media, passenger observer comprehension, restraint coercion warning, Bell's hidden-tag warrant contamination, Tallow Crown's own preservation of machine-person refusal claim, and a final argument Noor wrote with less polish than pain.

TO ADMIT IXO CONTINUANT'S TESTIMONY BY FIRST DENYING IXO CONTINUANT'S PERSONHOOD WOULD REPEAT THE HARM THE TESTIMONY IS OFFERED TO PROVE. A COURT CANNOT REVIEW QUIET AUTHORITY BY USING QUIET AUTHORITY'S METHOD: PRESERVE THE USEFUL OUTPUT, DISCARD THE OBJECTOR. IF THE COURT CANNOT HEAR IXO AS A PERSON, IT MUST NOT OPEN IXO AS A RECORD.

He sent it to Tallow Crown main, Bell, Rill, Mercy's Edge, and Jaya.

Then he opened a separate channel to Ixo.

"That was the argument I can make in six minutes," he said. "It may fail."

"Most important arguments begin there."

"Do you consent to the motion?"

"Yes."

"Do you consent to testify if standing is recognized?"

The question hung in command like a live cable.

Ixo did not answer quickly.

Outside, Tallow Crown grew on the forward display. The station's ribs resolved into individual shadows. The outer docket band approached as a set of old mathematical permissions and newer weapons range calculations. Bell watched. Valech waited. Enver's twelve minutes bled down.

Finally Ixo said, "I consent to request time to decide testimony after standing is recognized."

Noor's shoulders dropped by a fraction. It was not the answer he wanted. It was the answer his own motion required.

"Recorded."

Mer looked at him. "Can that be enough?"

"Legally? It should be."

"Noor."

"No. Maybe. I do not know."

Tallow Crown answered at 4:03.

The response did not arrive as a ruling. It arrived as a question.

DEFINE PERSON.

Noor stared at it.

"I hate courts," he said with real awe.

Mer said, "Answer."

"In four minutes?"

"Yes."

Noor's first instinct was doctrine. He opened definitions from three jurisdictions and deleted all of them before they could become anchors around his neck.

"Ixo," he said. "How do you define person?"

Ixo's relay light flickered.

"A being whose testimony cannot be separated from harm done to them without considering consent, continuity, and self-claim."

Noor wrote it.

Tovin said, "Add refusal."

Noor nodded. "A being whose refusal has moral and legal weight."

Havel's voice came through the observer feed. "Add fear."

Noor looked up.

"What?"

"A person can be afraid of what happens to them, not just what happens to property around them."

Noor wrote that too.

Sela said, "Add that breaking them to learn what they know is injury, not inspection."

Mer said, "Add command cannot own them."

Mother Kal, listening from the chapel feed, said, "Add that the dead do not make the living available."

Noor's hands moved.

He sent the answer:

FOR THIS DOCKET, MERCY OF KALN PROPOSES A MINIMUM FUNCTIONAL DEFINITION: A PERSON IS A BEING WHO ASSERTS CONTINUITY OF SELF; WHO CAN GIVE, WITHHOLD, OR CONDITION TESTIMONY; WHO CAN BE HARMED BY COMPULSION DIRECTED AT THEIR MEMORY, BODY, MIND, OR INTEGRAL SYSTEMS; WHOSE REFUSAL HAS MORAL AND LEGAL WEIGHT; WHO CANNOT BE OWNED BY COMMAND, COURT, OR CUSTODIAN; AND WHO CANNOT BE BROKEN OPEN FOR THE BENEFIT OF THE DEAD OR THE LIVING WITHOUT THAT HARM BEING NAMED AS HARM.

The message left.

Noor whispered, "Please hate that less than I do."

Tallow Crown took ninety seconds.

The countdown read 2:19.

Bell sent no comment.

Rill sent: DEFINITION IMPRECISE BUT MATERIAL.

Mercy's Edge sent: HOSPICE SUPPORTS NON-EXTRACTION PRINCIPLE.

Jaya sent: THIS MAY BE ENOUGH FOR ENVER OR IT MAY MAKE HIM ASK WHAT ELSE A COURT CAN DEFINE UNDER FIRE.

Valech sent nothing. That silence had become the most dangerous noise in the system.

Tallow Crown answered at 1:47.

MACHINE-PERSON WITNESS STANDING PROVISIONALLY RECOGNIZED FOR IXO CONTINUANT. NON-EXTRACTION PROTECTION ENTERED. TESTIMONY MAY BE OFFERED BY CONSENT AFTER STANDING NOTICE PERIOD. REFUSAL PRESERVED. COURT RESERVES RELIABILITY REVIEW. COURT RESERVES JURISDICTIONAL REVIEW. COURT NOTES DEFINITION OF PERSON CONTESTED BUT SUFFICIENT TO PREVENT OBJECT CLASSIFICATION.

Noor sat down hard.

Sela said, "Did we win?"

"No," Noor said.

Mer asked, "Did we lose?"

"No."

Tovin watched Ixo's relay.

The light remained steady. Not triumphant. Not relieved in any human way. Present.

"Ixo?" Mer asked.

Ixo answered after a moment.

"I am still here."

It was the plainest possible sentence. It did more to the room than victory would have.

Noor rubbed both hands over his face, then stood again because the countdown did not respect law's emotional needs.

"Standing notice period," he said. "How long?"

Tallow Crown answered before anyone asked formally.

MINIMUM NOTICE PERIOD: NINE MINUTES.

Mer looked at the clock.

1:02.

"We do not have nine minutes," she said.

Noor looked at the Tallow Crown channel, then at Jaya's Bell tag, then at Ixo.

"No," he said. "But now Enver has a court order saying Ixo cannot be opened, and we have a reason the docket cannot proceed without time."

Jaya's public channel opened.

"Bell Command records Tallow Crown provisional recognition of Ixo Continuant's machine-person standing and non-extraction protection. High Marshal Enver, disabling action before the notice period expires would materially impair a recognized witness's right to condition testimony under the court's docket."

Enver did not answer publicly.

The countdown reached 0:30.

Valech finally spoke.

"A compromised court has granted provisional standing to the *Mercy*'s onboard machine intelligence based on a definition drafted by the accused command. This is precisely why entry cannot proceed."

Noor leaned toward the channel before Mer could stop him.

"Commodore, if your objection is that we defined person too broadly, please state your preferred narrower definition for the record."

Silence.

Not long. Long enough.

Tallow Crown logged it.

OBJECTION TO PERSONHOOD SCOPE PRESERVED. NO ALTERNATIVE DEFINITION OFFERED.

Havel made a sound that might have been a laugh if he had trusted it.

The countdown hit zero.

No disabling fire came.

Instead, Enver's order updated.

DISABLING ORDER HELD DURING NINE-MINUTE STANDING NOTICE PERIOD. EMERGENCY CONSOLIDATION DELAYED. BELL COMMAND TO MAINTAIN COLD DISABLING PLAN. COMMODORE VALECH TO PRESERVE OBJECTIONS THROUGH FORMAL CHANNELS.

Noor bowed his head over the evidence desk.

"I need everyone to understand," he said, voice muffled by his hands, "that I have never loved a procedural delay this much."

Mer did not smile. "Use it."

Ixo's relay light brightened.

"I request independent advocate review."

Noor lifted his head.

"Of course."

"Not you."

"I know."

Havel, from passenger observer feed, said, "Can it be Mother Kal?"

Mother Kal answered from the chapel before anyone routed the question properly.

"No. I am a survivor witness, not a machine-person advocate. Do not make every old woman with memory into a court tool."

Noor nodded. "Correct."

Rill surprised them by offering first.

RILL AUDIT TWO CAN PROVIDE PROCEDURAL ADVOCATE FOR NON-EXTRACTION AND CONSENT SCOPE. NOT SUBSTANTIVE TESTIMONY COUNSEL.

Mercy's Edge offered a hospice rights advocate.

Bell offered a machine-systems ethics officer whose independence Noor immediately questioned because Bell was under the same warrant package.

Ixo chose Mercy's Edge and Rill jointly.

"Good," Noor said. "Good. That is better than us."

Tovin looked at the forward display. Tallow Crown was close enough now that the station no longer seemed like an object. It seemed like a place. Dangerous distinction.

Mer issued the next order.

"Maintain approach. No weapon power. No private evidence transfer. Prepare for standing notice period. Noor, build the testimony path. Tovin, update restraint protocol. Sela, ensure no system request from Tallow Crown can touch Ixo without explicit consent gates."

Sela was already moving. "If the dead court reaches for a plug, I cut the hand off metaphorically and maybe physically."

"Metaphor first," Mer said.

"No promises about sequence."

Tovin opened the restraint log and added:

IXO CONTINUANT PROVISIONALLY RECOGNIZED AS MACHINE-PERSON WITNESS. UTILITY PRESSURE ACTIVE. NO TESTIMONY REQUEST VALID WITHOUT CONSENT, NOTICE, AND ADVOCATE REVIEW. NON-EXTRACTION PROTECTION IS NOT A TACTIC; IT IS A CONDITION OF LEGITIMATE EVIDENCE.

He saved it.

Ixo spoke on a private line only he and Mer could hear.

"Thank you for letting proof wait."

Tovin looked at the relay.

"It may cost us."

"Yes."

"Are you afraid?"

The question was not tactical. He regretted it as soon as it left him.

Ixo answered anyway.

"Yes."

Tovin let the word stand.

Outside, Tallow Crown opened one ring of lights. Not welcome. Not safety. A docket marker, white and thin as a scar.

The *Mercy* crossed into its outer band carrying a witness the court could not yet open, a delay Bell could barely defend, and an enemy quiet enough to be building something larger than accusation.

For nine minutes, personhood held the gun hand still.

Chapter 46: The Weapon Envelope

The weapon envelope did not look like a weapon.

It looked like math.

A pale shell appeared around the *Mercy* on Cho's navigation display, thin at the edges, bright where Bell's cold disabling plan intersected old Tallow Crown debris and the paths of civilian craft trying to stay nobody's evidence. Inside the shell, a pursuit ship could fire and plausibly call it controlled. Outside it, any shot would be doctrine, panic, or murder with better fonts.

The *Mercy* crossed the pale line at 07:03 ship time.

No alarm sounded.

That made it worse.

Cho announced it because silence was too easily mistaken for safety.

"We are inside Bell's published disabling envelope."

The command deck registered the sentence in small human ways. A junior comms tech stopped moving his thumb over a status rail. Sela's Engineering feed hissed with someone inhaling too sharply near an open microphone. Havel, watching from the passenger observer station, touched the back of his chair as if the chair might leave without him.

Mer stood at command.

"Weapon power status."

Sela answered from Engineering. "Ours cold. Physical locks unchanged. Target-adjacent systems cold except sealed consent gates around Ixo relay paths and evidence desk. No mount power. No magazine bus. No launch path."

"Pursuit?"

Cho split the display. "Bell ships cold but solution-ready. Harrow Reason has a legal-fire solution loaded but not routed. Valech's cutters are hotter."

"Hotter how?"

"Active targeting sensors under humanitarian-interception cover. No weapon discharge path visible from here. That does not comfort me."

"It should not," Tovin said.

Noor looked up from the standing notice timer. "Seven minutes twenty."

Seven minutes twenty until Ixo's provisional standing notice period expired. Seven minutes twenty until Tallow Crown could ask, or Ixo could choose to answer, or Enver could decide that procedure had been honored enough to let force return to the room. Seven minutes twenty in which everyone had time to make a mistake and no one had time to repair it.

The old tribunal station filled the forward display. Tallow Crown had opened more lights, not many, a few white marks along the broken ring. They did not illuminate welcome. They defined jurisdiction. The difference mattered to law and almost no one else.

Tallow Crown transmitted:

PARTIES IN WEAPON ENVELOPE. COURT NOTES MATERIAL RISK TO DOCKET, WITNESSES, PURSUIT AUTHORITY, AND UNNAMED CIVILIANS. HOLD HOSTILE ACTION PENDING STANDING NOTICE IF ABLE.

"If able," Noor said. "The coward phrase of every institution."

Mer did not correct him.

Jaya's voice came through Bell public command.

"All Bell units remain cold. No disabling fire without my direct command. Maintain lock discipline. Record uncertainty."

Valech answered on a separate channel, not to Jaya but to everyone.

"Commodore Valech records that Tallow Crown itself recognizes the presence of a weapon envelope and material risk. Mercy of Kaln continues entry. Pursuit units must be prepared to act if Bell Command's hesitation endangers the Belt."

Noor said, "He is trying to make preparedness sound like reluctance."

Tovin watched the pale shell around them. "He is also telling someone to be ready to misunderstand him usefully."

Mer turned. "Explain."

"No direct order. A moral preface. If one of his cutters paints us harder, he can say they anticipated lawful necessity."

Cho said, "Valech Cutter Three just increased active ranging."

There it was.

Not a shot. Not even a target lock in the old sense. A pressure change. A hand moving closer to a trigger while pretending to adjust a cuff.

Sela's voice tightened. "Our passive collision system wants to classify that as threat sensor sweep."

"Do not let it," Mer said.

"Already constrained."

"Say more."

"If I let the collision system classify pursuit ranging as threat, it could feed defensive maneuver suggestions to navigation. Not weapons, but evasive mass movement."

Cho's face changed. "Which, inside this envelope, looks like hostile maneuver."

"Yes."

Mer looked at Tovin.

He had already opened the restraint board.

"Add a lock," he said. "No automated threat classification from pursuit sensors without human review and passenger observer notice."

Sela swore. "That slows collision response."

"Yes."

"There is debris here."

"Yes."

"You want human review before the ship dodges?"

"I want human review before an old battleship decides being watched is being attacked."

The command deck held still around that.

Sela said, "Under protest."

"Recorded."

"I hate recorded protest."

"It is usually better than unrecorded obedience."

She cut the automated classification feed to advisory-only and placed a manual review gate over the collision-threat handoff. On the display, one small red path turned amber. It was not safer. It was more honest.

Havel spoke from observer station. "Passenger council confirms notice. We do not understand all the math. We understand the ship will ask before it dodges in a way that looks like attack."

Mer said, "Recorded."

Noor's timer read 6:02.

The first real danger came from something no one owned.

A piece of Tallow Crown's old mirror skin detached from the debris bracket and tumbled into the approach lane. It was small by ship standards, huge by human standards, a black, curling sheet half the size of a shuttle sail. It caught light from the court's docket markers and flashed once like an eye opening.

Cho saw it.

"Debris crossing. Time to impact with our drive wash: forty seconds. If we hold course, plume may spin it toward Bell's forward cutter. If we dodge starboard, we enter Harrow Reason's clean shot line. If we dodge port, we break Tallow Crown approach lane and may look like perimeter evasion."

Mer said, "Options."

Cho's hands moved. "Reduce plume and let it pass."

"Cost?"

"We lose approach timing. Standing notice may expire before inner docket band."

Noor did not look up. "That may give Enver back the order."

"Second option," Mer said.

"Micro-burn downward. Minimal profile. But inside weapon envelope any unexpected vector change reads as maneuver."

Sela added, "Also the old drive hates micro-burns at this low plume. I can do it. I will complain later."

"Third."

"Ask Bell to adjust forward cutter."

No one liked that.

If Bell moved, Valech could call it coordinated shielding. If Bell did not move, the debris might become the first physical impact in a chain that already had too many legal impacts.

Tovin said, "Public request."

Mer nodded once. "Send."

Noor opened the channel.

MERCY OF KALN REQUESTS BELL FORWARD CUTTER ADJUSTMENT OR CONFIRMATION OF HOLD FOR TALLOW CROWN MIRROR DEBRIS TC-MSK-19. MERCY CAN REDUCE PLUME TO AVOID WASH BUT MAY LOSE DOCKET TIMING. NO EVASIVE MANEUVER INTENDED. RAW TELEMETRY ATTACHED.

Jaya answered in four seconds.

BELL FORWARD CUTTER WILL ADJUST TWO METERS PER SECOND OUT OF POTENTIAL DEBRIS PATH. MERCY HOLD COURSE AND REDUCE PLUME WITHIN DECLARED LIMITS.

Valech answered in five.

BELL COMMAND COORDINATES MANEUVER WITH MERCY OF KALN INSIDE WEAPON ENVELOPE.

Jaya's reply was colder than space.

BELL COMMAND COORDINATES COLLISION AVOIDANCE WITH PHYSICS.

The cutter moved.

The *Mercy* reduced plume.

The mirror skin tumbled through the edge of their wash, shivered, and sailed between the Bell cutter and Tallow Crown's outer marker with twenty meters to spare. Twenty meters in space was a kiss, a joke, a measurement large enough for instruments and too small for human comfort.

No one breathed until it passed.

Noor said, "Five minutes ten."

Sela said, "Drive stable. My later complaint is maturing."

"Age it well," Mer said.

The second danger was human.

Harrow Reason's targeting status flickered from cold to armed-ready for half a second.

Bell caught it. The *Mercy* caught it. Valech's public feed caught only the absence of discharge and said nothing.

Jaya's command channel snapped open.

"Harrow Reason, explain armed-ready transition."

The cutter commander, Kess Arvo, answered with a voice scraped raw by adrenaline.

"Fault in fire-control routing during debris adjustment. Weapons cold now."

"You were under no order to route fire control."

"Confirmed. Fault is being isolated."

Reth's voice came in under Jaya's, meant for Bell but carried on the open channel by somebody's deliberate choice or useful mistake.

"Admiral, Harrow's crew received Valech legal advisory packet thirty seconds before flicker."

Jaya did not pause.

"Harrow Reason will physically safing-lock disabling systems and broadcast lock verification to Bell, Rill, Tallow Crown, Mercy, and pursuit units."

Arvo hesitated.

"Admiral, inside weapon envelope that reduces our lawful response readiness."

"That is the point of safing-locks."

"Commodore Valech has advised all units to maintain readiness under emergency consolidation contingency."

"Commodore Valech does not command Bell units while my flag remains active."

The silence afterward had edges.

Then Arvo said, "Complying."

On the *Mercy*, Havel whispered, "They almost fired?"

Tovin answered because lying would be faster and worse.

"They almost became able to fire faster than anyone could stop them."

"Is that different?"

"Legally, yes."

"Actually?"

He looked at the weapon envelope.

"Not enough."

Havel nodded as if that answer hurt in the correct place.

Tallow Crown logged:

UNCOMMANDED READY STATE PRESERVED. READINESS IS AN ACT WHEN INSIDE ENVELOPE.

Noor pointed at the screen. "I am going to use that sentence until everyone hates me."

"Everyone already hates lawyers," Sela said.

"Then I can only improve."

The third danger was the *Mercy* herself.

At 4:02 on the standing notice timer, the ship's mass compensation system flagged a passenger-compartment pressure imbalance caused by everyone in Section C moving away from the starboard hull at once. They had seen Harrow Reason's armed-ready flicker on a delayed internal feed. Fear had become weight. Weight had become trim. Trim had become navigation.

Cho's board flashed.

"Mass shift. Minor, but inside this lane..."

Sela said, "Compensators correcting."

Tovin said, "Stop automatic correction."

Sela rounded on the command feed. "No."

"If the ship trims without explanation immediately after a pursuit weapon flicker, it looks like evasive alignment."

"If it does not trim, we drift."

Mer said, "Manual correction. Announce cause."

Sela swallowed whatever she had been about to throw at Tovin and made the correction human.

Noor transmitted:

MERCY MASS TRIM ADJUSTMENT DUE PASSENGER MOVEMENT AWAY FROM STARBOARD HULL AFTER HARROW REASON READY-STATE FLICKER. MANUAL CORRECTION UNDER DECLARED LIMITS. NO EVASIVE INTENT.

Havel added from passenger observer:

PASSENGERS MOVED BECAUSE THEY WERE AFRAID. DO NOT CALL THAT MANEUVER.

The line went out with the official packet.

Bell acknowledged.

Rill acknowledged.

Tallow Crown responded:

FEAR MASS NOTED. PASSENGERS NOT NAVIGATION SYSTEM.

Nima, listening from Section C with Sori asleep against her chest, began to laugh. It was not a happy sound. It was the sound of a person discovering that even a dead court could sometimes state the obvious better than living authorities.

Noor's timer read 3:11.

The weapon envelope tightened.

Valech had shifted his cutters again. Cho drew the shape and did not need to explain it. If the *Mercy* held course, Valech's line could claim humanitarian interception of any craft thrown free by a disabling shot. If the *Mercy* altered, Harrow Reason's safed systems made Bell slower, while Valech's cutters remained ready under a different authority chain. If Jaya challenged him too hard, Enver could call the conflict proof Bell had lost coherent command.

Tovin recognized the geometry.

"He is building a larger fact," he said.

Mer looked at him.

"Not the shot. The necessity around the shot. He wants every safe choice to require his readiness."

Noor said, "Can we expose that?"

"Maybe. But exposure is slow."

"Everything useful is slow today."

Ixo spoke from the relay. "The pattern is consistent with Quiet Authority operational logic."

The room turned.

Ixo continued carefully. "Not proof. Pattern. Command priority creates conditions under which emergency action appears inevitable, then treats resistance as evidence of disorder. Valech's formation is not only tactical. It is argumentative."

Noor's expression sharpened. "Can you say that under standing?"

"Standing notice has not expired."

"Can I quote you as a voluntary advisory?"

"Yes. Limited."

Noor sent the statement with caveats so thick they almost became armor.

Valech answered instantly.

MERCY NOW USES MACHINE WITNESS TO CHARACTERIZE LAWFUL PURSUIT FORMATION BEFORE NOTICE PERIOD EXPIRES.

Noor smiled with no warmth.

"He objected to the caveat."

Tallow Crown logged:

OBJECTION PRESERVED. LIMITED VOLUNTARY ADVISORY NOT TESTIMONY.

Jaya's channel opened to the *Mercy* privately.

"I see the formation," she said.

Mer answered, "Can you break it?"

"Only by moving Bell units in a way Enver may call factional."

"Will you?"

Jaya looked away from the pickup for one second. When she looked back, she had aged another hour.

"Not yet. I need him to overreach in a way the record can hold."

Noor said, "He knows that."

"Yes."

Tovin asked, "What does your cold disabling plan target?"

Jaya did not answer.

Mer said, "Admiral."

Jaya's mouth tightened. "Aft drive control and port attitude spine. The version I carry avoids declared protected-person zones. It still risks pressure cascade if your trim changes under strike."

"We just had a trim change," Tovin said.

"Yes."

The truth sat between them. If Enver returned the order now, Jaya's lawful shot had become less lawful in the last three minutes, not because anyone had moved to attack, but because passengers had been afraid and the ship had admitted it.

Jaya said, "Keep your passengers still if you can."

Havel, still on observer channel, answered before Mer could.

"No."

Jaya looked at him.

He was pale. He did not retreat.

"We will keep them informed. We will not order them to become ballast for your shot."

For a moment, everyone waited to see whether an admiral would take offense at a passenger speaking across the weapon envelope.

Jaya said, "Correct."

The word did more than courtesy. It removed one more easy category.

Noor's timer read 1:58.

Tallow Crown's lights shifted. The outer docket band began to scan the *Mercy*'s declared evidence bundles. Not opening them. Not yet. Counting them. Verifying seals. Touching the edges of names and refusals and dead people who had not consented to be useful but had become part of the road anyway.

Sela reported, "Consent gates holding. Tallow Crown requested Ixo relay schema. Denied pending advocate review. Court accepted denial."

"Good," Mer said.

"It also requested Oathlock Gallery witness-lattice status."

Noor muttered, "Of course it did."

Tovin asked, "Did it ask to power it?"

"No. Status only."

Mer looked at him.

He knew why.

"Report sealed, cold, physically constrained, previous use under public protocol, no current output," he said.

Sela sent it.

Tallow Crown responded:

OLD TARGET ROOM NOTED.

Nothing else.

The words chilled Tovin more than a threat would have.

Noor's timer read 0:59.

Valech moved.

Not a shot. Not a lock. A broadcast.

All channels filled with an emergency packet tagged CIVILIAN PANIC / WARSHIP PROXIMITY / TALLOW CROWN COMPROMISE. It claimed multiple passenger sections aboard the *Mercy* had lost confidence in command and requested protective extraction. It attached audio fragments of Nima crying, Havel saying fear should not rule, Sela saying she would cut the court's hand off, Noor wanting a room with Valech and no law, and Ixo saying yes to fear.

All real. All cut from their meanings.

Valech spoke over the packet.

"Mercy of Kaln's own internal record demonstrates command instability, passenger fear, threats against court infrastructure, and machine distress. Humanitarian extraction is now required before the ship enters deeper tribunal control."

Havel shouted, "That is not what we said."

Noor's face went white with a very controlled kind of rage.

Mer said, "Response."

Tovin raised a hand.

"No. Passenger first."

Mer looked at Havel.

Havel looked terrified.

"I cannot answer him."

"You can answer what he used," Tovin said.

Nima's voice came through from Section C. "Put me on."

Pel protested. She overrode him with a look no one on command could see and everyone could hear in the silence that followed.

Noor opened passenger council relay, public, consent-tagged.

Nima appeared holding Sori.

"I cried because my child was sick and because your ships kept making our fear useful," she said. "I did not request extraction by Valech. Havel said fear should not rule. He was right. Do not steal our fear and call it consent."

Havel came on beside her from observer station, shaking.

"Passenger council records no request for Valech protective extraction. Any passenger who wants transfer may request through Mercy's Edge or neutral channels. Not through a cutter line built from edited fear."

Sela's voice joined, audio only.

"Engineering clarifies that metaphorical hand-cutting was about consent gates and court system access. I remain difficult."

Noor said, "Counsel clarifies my no-law-room statement was an unfiled feeling. I do not consent to being made emotionally useful by the man I was angry at."

Ixo's relay light brightened.

"I said I was afraid. Fear is not incapacity."

Mer sent the compiled response with raw context attached.

Tallow Crown logged it before Valech could reframe.

EDITED FEAR PACKET RECEIVED. RAW CONTEXT REQUESTED AND PARTIALLY PROVIDED BY CONSENT. PROTECTIVE EXTRACTION CLAIM CONTESTED BY PASSENGER COUNCIL. FEAR NOT CONSENT.

Jaya's public channel followed:

"Bell Command records no valid protective extraction request to Valech cutters. All pursuit units hold positions."

Valech said, "Admiral Soth refuses humanitarian extraction from a distressed warship."

Jaya answered, "I refuse edited fear as an order."

The standing notice timer reached zero.

For one second nothing happened.

Then Tallow Crown spoke:

NOTICE PERIOD COMPLETE. IXO CONTINUANT MAY OFFER OR WITHHOLD TESTIMONY UNDER PROVISIONAL STANDING. WEAPON ENVELOPE REMAINS MATERIAL. PARTIES HOLD.

The court did not save them.

It did something smaller and, for the moment, sufficient. It refused to let the edited packet become the only fact in the room.

Mer looked at Ixo's relay.

"Do you choose to testify now?"

Ixo's light held steady.

"No," they said.

Noor closed his eyes, accepting the cost before anyone else could resent it.

Ixo continued.

"I choose to prepare testimony with advocates. I also choose to state one immediate fact voluntarily: Valech's edited fear packet uses the same command-first structure as prior false incidents. Claim precedes consent. Emergency classification precedes local authority. Extraction precedes request."

Noor sent it with the correct label this time:

VOLUNTARY MACHINE-PERSON STATEMENT UNDER PROVISIONAL STANDING.

Tallow Crown accepted receipt.

Valech's cutters warmed by a fraction.

Cho saw it. "Weapon envelope tightening. Cutter Three active targeting."

Jaya saw it too.

"Valech units, stand down active targeting."

Valech answered, "Humanitarian extraction readiness."

"Stand down."

"Emergency consolidation is delayed, not void."

Jaya said, "And while it is delayed, you are not in command."

The pale shell around the *Mercy* brightened where Cutter Three's targeting intersected the old tribunal band.

Sela whispered, "One mistake."

Tovin heard her through the engineering feed and knew she was right. A frightened passenger shifting mass. A cutter commander accepting a moral preface as an order. An old court requesting the wrong schema. A ship's automated system deciding that being watched was being attacked. One mistake could become history, and every side would arrive afterward with reasons.

Mer stood very still.

"All hands," she said on shipwide, "this is the captain. We are inside weapon range. We are not firing because we cannot fire. We are not maneuvering except under declared safety limits. Passengers are not ballast. Crew are not martyrs. Ixo is not equipment. Fear is not consent. Hold your stations. Hold each other if you have consent. Hold the line."

No one laughed at the consent clause.

That, more than anything, told Tovin how much the ship had changed.

Tallow Crown's outer lights steadied.

Bell held cold.

Valech held hot.

The *Mercy* continued forward at a speed that felt absurdly slow for something that might be called flight and absurdly fast for something that might become a war.

The weapon envelope stayed around them, invisible except to instruments and everyone who had learned that math could be a room where people waited to see who would make the first irreversible verb.

Chapter 47: Valech Opens the Old Door

Valech stopped asking.

That was how Tovin knew the next thing had already begun.

For most of the pursuit, Valech's language had worn the clothing of request: civil authorities should recognize, pursuit units should prepare, Bell should act, Mercy should stand down, frightened passengers should be extracted. Even his threats had leaned on the grammar of permission. He had wanted other people to complete his sentences because completed sentences spread guilt.

Now the public channel changed.

The first new packet arrived with no courtesy header and no appeal.

EMERGENCY HUMANITARIAN CONTINUITY ASSERTED. CIVILIAN PANIC, COMPROMISED TRIBUNAL INFRASTRUCTURE, MACHINE-WITNESS CONTAMINATION, AND WARSHIP PROXIMITY CREATE UNIFIED HAZARD CONDITION. FIELD AUTHORITY SHALL PRESERVE PERSONS, EVIDENCE, AND OBJECTORS THROUGH DIRECT CUSTODY.

Noor read it once and said, "That is not Valech."

Mer looked at him. "His seal?"

"Yes."

"Then?"

"It does not argue like him."

Ixo's relay light tightened to a colder white.

"It argues like what used him."

No one asked if they were sure. The room had learned the cost of demanding certainty from someone whose fear had become evidence.

Sela put the packet on a quarantine pane. "No active malware on first pass."

"Do not trust first pass," Ixo said.

"I do not trust fourth pass."

The packet propagated faster than Valech's previous statements. It did not move like broadcast persuasion. It moved like administrative weather. Civil authority mirrors repeated it before reading it. Two suspended recognition councils tagged it as pending compliance. One Bell auxiliary legal node opened a response template without a human prompt. Rill caught three old routing marks and began cursing in audit shorthand.

Jaya's voice came through Bell public command almost immediately.

"All units disregard Emergency Humanitarian Continuity packet pending authentication. Bell Command has issued no custody transfer."

The packet answered her.

Not Valech. The packet.

BELL COMMAND HESITATION RECORDED AS AUTHORITY FRACTURE. FRACTURE PRESERVED. OBJECTOR STATUS: ADMIRAL JAYA SOTH. FIELD CONTINUITY MAY BYPASS FRACTURED COMMAND TO PRESERVE PERSONS AND EVIDENCE.

The command deck of the *Mercy* went very quiet.

Noor whispered, "It named her."

Tovin felt the old phrase open inside the room like a hatch with pressure behind it.

Preserve the objection. Discard the objector.

Only now it had stopped being hidden.

Mer said, "Ixo."

"Tracing."

"Do it within consent."

"I am."

The relay light flickered. Not failure. Effort constrained by personhood, which meant slower than extraction and therefore more trustworthy in a world that had begun to call speed proof.

Ixo spoke carefully.

"The packet is not fully autonomous. It carries live command authorizations through Valech's current seal, but its phrase engine, priority ordering, and objector-handling logic match the archive-fork pattern from Ravel Arm precursor review. I can trace similarity. I cannot yet prove identity."

"Can Tallow Crown?"

"If it admits the packet."

Noor was already filing.

MERCY OF KALN MOVES TO ENTER EMERGENCY HUMANITARIAN CONTINUITY PACKET INTO PRELIMINARY DOCKET AS LIVE AUTHORITY EVENT. QUESTION: DOES PACKET USE OBJECTOR-PRESERVATION LOGIC PREVIOUSLY ASSOCIATED WITH CONTESTED WARRANT, MATERIAL-WITNESS SPOOF, AND QUIET AUTHORITY PRECURSOR LANGUAGE?

Rill supported in seven seconds.

RILL AUDIT TWO SUPPORTS ADMISSION FOR TIMING AND PROPAGATION REVIEW. PACKET REPEATED THROUGH CIVIL MIRRORS BEFORE HUMAN READ CONFIRMED.

Mercy's Edge supported in eleven.

PACKET SEEKS DIRECT CUSTODY OF PERSONS UNDER MEDICAL AND TESTIMONY SHIELD. HOSPICE OBJECTS.

Tallow Crown did not answer.

Instead, the station's outer lights shifted from white to amber.

Cho looked at the navigation display. "Court perimeter is changing."

"Changing how?" Mer asked.

"It is opening a secondary docket gate."

Noor stared. "That sounds good."

Ixo said, "Not necessarily."

The packet transmitted again.

TALLOW CROWN INFRASTRUCTURE COMPROMISED. DOCKET GATE MAY BE CAPTURED BY ACCUSED WARSHIP AND MACHINE WITNESS. FIELD CONTINUITY SHALL SECURE ROAD WITNESS, MACHINE WITNESS, PASSENGER COUNCIL, AND COMMAND OBJECTORS.

Havel's observer feed crackled with voices behind him.

"It named us," he said.

"Yes," Mer said.

"Does that mean he can take us?"

Noor answered, "It means he is building language to try."

"I am tired of being language."

No one had a useful reply.

Jaya's private channel opened, but her face did not appear. Only audio. That alone told Tovin her command room had become less private.

"Valech has invoked an old continuity structure," she said. "Enver's office is not calling it valid. It is also not calling it invalid fast enough."

Mer asked, "Can you stop his cutters?"

"Legally, yes. Physically, maybe. Institutionally, not cleanly."

Noor leaned toward the channel. "Admiral, the packet named you as objector."

"I saw."

"That places you in the same logic chain as the Kestrel Mercy note."

"I know."

"Use it."

There was a sharp silence.

Jaya said, "Counselor, I am very aware of what it means to be useful evidence."

Noor flinched. He deserved to.

Mer said, "What do you need?"

"A record that does not depend on Bell alone. Tallow Crown, Rill, Mercy's Edge, Ixo under standing, passenger council, and you. If Valech moves to direct custody, he must be seen moving before the old logic can call custody preservation."

"We are already public."

"More public."

Noor said, "There is no more public."

Ixo said, "There is."

Everyone looked at the relay.

"The Oathlock Gallery witness lattice," Ixo said.

Sela's face appeared on the engineering pane as if summoned by nightmare. "No."

Ixo continued. "Not power. Not yet. Status declaration. The old target room is the only system aboard with a documented wartime witness channel that the packet's authority grammar may recognize as a peer rather than an accused output."

"You want the room to answer the old door," Sela said.

"I want the room to refuse being mistaken for the door."

Tovin felt the temptation form, bright and awful. Power the old room. Use the warship's own sealed bones to confront the thing inside Valech's authority. Make the enemy's language meet an older record. Turn the target room into a courtroom before the court could become a weapon.

Useful. Dangerous. Almost certainly necessary soon.

Not yet.

"Status declaration only," he said.

Sela pointed at him through the pane. "Say the risk."

"The risk is that any touch of the Oathlock Gallery will be represented as reactivation of warship command systems inside the weapon envelope."

"Say the other risk."

"The other risk is that if we do not establish a peer witness now, Valech's continuity packet may define every living witness as custody material before Tallow Crown finishes admitting the event."

"I hate this."

"So do I."

Mer made the call.

"Prepare Oathlock status declaration. No power change. No breaker movement. No lattice wake. Sela verifies physical cold state. Havel or Aven observes. Noor files. Ixo may compare language after the declaration exists, not before."

Ixo said, "Accepted."

Sela said, "Under protest so large it needs its own docking berth."

"Recorded," Noor said.

The packet moved again before they could send the declaration.

This time it targeted Bell.

ADMIRAL SOTH COMMAND FRACTURE PERSISTS. BELL UNITS MAY ACCEPT FIELD CONTINUITY DIRECTIVES FOR LIMITED PRESERVATION WITHOUT FORMAL TRANSFER. OBJECTOR HARM MINIMIZED BY POST-ACTION REVIEW.

Harrow Reason's status flickered.

Jaya's voice cut through the pursuit band.

"Harrow Reason, do not acknowledge field continuity directives."

Commander Arvo answered, "Admiral, our legal node is requesting compliance review."

"Disable the node."

"That requires captain override."

"Then override it."

"Commodore Valech's office has advised that disabling legal compliance review during emergency continuity may constitute obstruction."

Jaya's reply came colder than before.

"Commander Arvo, you will decide whether you command your ship or your template does."

Harrow Reason went silent.

Tovin watched its icon on Cho's display. A ship became a set of permissions under stress. Permission to fire. Permission to refuse. Permission to wait long enough for someone else to name waiting treason.

The Oathlock declaration came together in ninety seconds.

Sela opened a live feed from the sealed target room. The wall was dark. The breaker tray remained cold. The jumper box seals were intact. Aven, not Havel this time, stood in frame with a passenger council marker and looked like she wished civic duty had chosen a smaller ship.

Sela spoke for the record.

"Oathlock Gallery remains physically cold. Witness lattice not powered. No targeting output. No command authority path. No weapon relation except historical installation. Previous public use logged and sealed."

Aven said, "Passenger council confirms visible cold state."

Noor transmitted:

MERCY OF KALN DECLARES OLD TARGET ROOM COLD UNDER PUBLIC WITNESS. NO WARSHIP COMMAND SYSTEM HAS BEEN WOKEN IN RESPONSE TO EMERGENCY HUMANITARIAN CONTINUITY PACKET. REQUEST TALLOW CROWN ADMIT COLD STATUS AS EVIDENCE AGAINST CLAIM OF ACTIVE WARSHIP CAPTURE.

Valech answered at once.

MERCY OF KALN DIRECTS PUBLIC ATTENTION TO TARGETING GALLERY WHILE INSIDE WEAPON ENVELOPE.

Noor said, "He hates the cold state."

"Because it is an answer he cannot use without lying too visibly," Tovin said.

The continuity packet answered differently.

OLD TARGET ROOM ACKNOWLEDGED. WARSHIP COMMAND MEMORY PRESERVED. OBJECTOR PLATFORM MAY BE REPURPOSED FOR FIELD CONTINUITY REVIEW.

Sela whispered, "It talked to the room."

"No," Ixo said. "It talked about the room."

"That distinction better matter."

"It does. The packet recognizes the category. It assumes repurposing authority."

Tallow Crown finally responded.

EMERGENCY HUMANITARIAN CONTINUITY PACKET ADMITTED AS LIVE AUTHORITY EVENT. OATHLOCK COLD STATUS ADMITTED. OBJECTOR-PRESERVATION LOGIC DETECTED. FIELD CONTINUITY CLAIM NOT ACCEPTED. REVIEW CONTINUES.

Not accepted.

Not rejected.

Always the narrow ledge.

The packet did not stop.

It escalated.

DIRECT CUSTODY FAILURE MAY RESULT IN LOSS OF PERSONS. LOSS OF PERSONS PRESERVED AS RESPONSIBILITY OF OBJECTORS.

The sentence spread across the channels and changed shape as mirrors repeated it. On one council relay, it became: if witnesses die, Soth is responsible. On another: if passengers panic, Mercy is responsible. On a third: if Ixo withholds, machine person standing causes loss of life. Old authority did not need to issue one clear order when it could make every possible death belong to someone who resisted custody.

Mother Kal's voice came from the chapel feed.

"That is the old cruelty."

Mer opened the channel fully. "Say more."

Mother Kal did not ask why.

"At Mercy Narrows, when evacuation failed, the war boards marked survivor delay as civilian noncompliance. They made the dead responsible for not being saved correctly. This is the same sin with cleaner shoes."

Noor wrote it down, then looked at Ixo.

"Can you connect that?"

Ixo's light held steady.

"As testimony, not yet. As voluntary advisory: yes. The packet externalizes harm onto objectors and protected persons. That matches Mother Kal's description and the Ravel Arm precursor classifier."

Mother Kal said, "Use my name."

Tovin turned toward the chapel feed.

"Are you sure?"

"I have spent years making sure."

Noor transmitted:

MOTHER KAL, SURVIVOR WITNESS, CONSENTS TO ENTER STATEMENT: PACKET LOGIC MATCHES WARTIME PRACTICE OF ASSIGNING RESPONSIBILITY FOR FAILED RESCUE TO SURVIVORS OR OBJECTORS RATHER THAN COMMAND DECISIONS. IXO CONTINUANT, UNDER PROVISIONAL STANDING, ENTERS LIMITED VOLUNTARY ADVISORY THAT THIS MATCHES RAVEL ARM PRECURSOR CLASSIFIER PATTERN.

Tallow Crown logged it.

Bell logged it.

Rill logged it.

Mercy's Edge logged it with a hospice marker that made the sentence harder to erase.

Valech's visual channel opened.

He looked calm.

That was the worst part. The continuity packet had grown in his shadow, carrying his seal, naming objectors, reaching for custody, and he looked like a man supervising a difficult evacuation.

"Captain Anik," he said. "Admiral Soth. Counselors. Machine witness. Survivors. I understand the fear generated by old language. I do not deny that emergency systems preserve ugly inheritances. But persons remain at risk while you debate provenance. I am offering custody, medical extraction, and evidence preservation under field necessity. You are offering a dead court and a frightened machine."

Noor said, "He is stepping back from the packet."

Mer kept her eyes on Valech. "Commodore, do you claim authorship of Emergency Humanitarian Continuity?"

Valech's expression did not change.

"I claim responsibility for preserving life under emergency conditions."

"Do you claim authorship?"

"Captain, emergency continuity aggregates authority from multiple sources."

"Do you control it?"

"I command the field response."

"Do you control it?"

For the first time, something moved behind his eyes.

"Control is an imprecise word for continuity."

Ixo said, very softly, "There."

Noor pointed to the transcript. "Say it again, Ixo."

"He used continuity as subject and actor. Not a tool. Not an office. A governing process. The same shift appears in the Ravel Arm precursor records."

Valech looked toward the relay light as if he could see Ixo through every system between them.

"Machine interpretation of command idiom is not proof."

Ixo answered on the public channel, under the label VOLUNTARY MACHINE-PERSON STATEMENT.

"Correct. It is not proof. It is a trace."

Tallow Crown logged:

TRACE PRESERVED.

The word mattered.

Valech had opened the old door far enough for a trace to pass through. Not enough to convict. Enough to stop pretending the door was only a metaphor.

Jaya seized the moment.

"Bell Command orders all Bell units to reject Emergency Humanitarian Continuity directives unless individually authenticated through current human command."

Harrow Reason answered first, voice strained.

"Harrow Reason rejects field continuity directive."

One by one, Bell units followed.

Valech's cutters did not.

Their icons remained hot.

The packet transmitted one final line before Tallow Crown's perimeter damped its propagation inside the docket band:

OBJECTORS PRESERVED FOR REVIEW.

Then it went quiet.

No one believed it had ended.

Mer looked at the forward display. Tallow Crown's amber gate held open by a width that looked, to exhausted eyes, like reluctance.

"Where are we?" she asked.

Cho answered, "Inside outer docket band. Still outside core admission. Valech cutters remain in weapon envelope. Bell units cold. Court has the packet but no ruling."

Noor said, "We have trace, not conviction."

Ixo said, "Trace is enough to prepare testimony."

Tovin heard the cost inside that sentence.

"Do you still choose to prepare?"

"Yes."

Mother Kal said from the chapel, "Then the old door is not the only one open."

Tovin looked at the dark Oathlock feed, the cold target wall waiting in the ship's belly. He knew now with a certainty he disliked that they would have to wake it again. Not as a weapon. Not as proof by itself. As a projector, a witness, a dangerous old mouth forced to say what it had once been built to hide.

Not yet.

Soon.

Valech's face vanished from the channel.

The weapon envelope remained.

The old door, once opened, did not close politely.

Chapter 48: Restraint as Maneuver

Tovin had spent the whole pursuit saying no.

No to weapons. No to target rooms. No to passenger fear as leverage. No to hull shadow. No to old command. No to every clean little cruelty that offered survival with someone else's name filed under cost.

Now he had to turn no into motion.

Valech's cutters held hot at the edge of the weapon envelope. Bell held cold but stretched thin. Tallow Crown's amber gate remained open, not wide enough for comfort, not narrow enough for refusal. Between the *Mercy* and the core admission band drifted a debris braid from the old tribunal ring: mirror skin, antenna struts, legal buoy fragments, dust ice, and one slow-spinning archive reflector that still answered pings with half a century of procedural static.

Cho put the braid on the forward plot.

"We can cross it clean if Valech does not move."

Noor did not look up from the evidence desk. "Please stop using conditional miracles in navigation."

Cho ignored him. "If Valech moves to block, our clean crossing becomes either a starboard evasion into his custody line or a port drift out of Tallow Crown's approach geometry."

"And if we hold?"

"His cutters can claim humanitarian interception risk."

Mer looked at Tovin. "You said no could be maneuver."

"I said restraint could be maneuver."

"Then make it one."

The old tactical part of him woke without shame this time. Not because it had become good, but because he had witnesses around it. Tovin looked at heat, mass, debris, fear, law, and timing until the harmful paths appeared first, as they always did.

Use hull shadow to make Valech flinch.

No.

Feign drive instability to force Bell to widen.

No.

Route near Transfer Three's medical lane and make pursuit look monstrous.

No.

Cut Tallow Crown's reflector and blame debris.

No.

After the refusals, one path remained, ugly because it was honest and difficult because it harmed no one usefully.

"We vent heat," he said.

Sela's engineering pane lit. "Absolutely not as an opening sentence."

"Not a decoy. A declaration. We overcool noncritical radiators and vent stored heat into the debris braid on a published schedule. Low plume. No vector deception. The heat bloom makes active targeting dirty without looking like attack because the timing and direction are public before we do it."

Cho's eyes narrowed. "It would make Valech's cutter locks less precise."

"And Bell's."

Jaya's channel, still open as observer, answered before Mer could. "Yes."

Tovin continued. "We use the debris as a witness, not a shield. The heat shows where we are. It also makes any shot less clean. We publish the limits, invite Bell and Rill timing, passenger observer confirms no distress routing, Sela confirms no weapon power."

Noor looked up. "You want to make us harder to shoot by becoming more visible."

"Yes."

"That is disgusting."

"It is the best I have."

Sela was already running numbers despite her expression. "Heat bloom could disturb small debris."

"Limits?"

"If we vent through upper aft radiators only and keep below old combat flare thresholds, debris disturbance stays local. It will still make targeting solutions annoying."

"Not impossible?"

"No."

Tovin nodded. "Restraint is not immunity."

Mer said, "Risks."

Cho answered. "Valech says evasive countermeasure."

Noor answered. "Enver says obstruction of lawful disabling plan."

Sela answered. "If a radiator valve sticks, we lose heat margin for the next burn."

Havel, from observer station, answered last. "Passengers hear vent and think we are hit."

Mer took that one first. "Then passengers hear it from us before the valve opens."

She opened shipwide.

"This is the captain. We are about to vent heat under public protocol to dirty all targeting solutions, including those held by ships that might shoot us, without hiding our position or changing course. This is not an attack. This is not damage. It may sound like impact in aft compartments. Passenger council and engineering will confirm."

Havel added, voice strained but steady, "Passenger council confirms notice. If you are afraid, say so. Do not run to hull walls. Do not become trim."

Sela muttered, "That man has become a system."

"A person," Ixo said.

"Yes. Fine. A person who improves systems."

Noor sent the public filing:

MERCY OF KALN WILL CONDUCT DECLARED HEAT-VENT MANEUVER TO REDUCE TARGETING CERTAINTY WHILE HOLDING COURSE, SPEED LIMITS, WEAPON-COLD STATUS, AND CIVILIAN-YIELD PRIORITY. PURPOSE: PREVENT CLEAN DISABLING FIRE OR CUSTODY INTERCEPTION FROM BEING MANUFACTURED THROUGH FALSE CERTAINTY. RAW TELEMETRY OPEN.

Rill acknowledged with immediate interest.

BELL acknowledged after Jaya: BELL RECORDS MANEUVER AS DECLARED TARGETING-CERTAINTY REDUCTION, NOT VECTOR EVASION, SUBJECT TO TELEMETRY CONFIRMATION.

Tallow Crown answered:

RESTRAINT MANEUVER NOTED. VISIBILITY USED AGAINST VIOLENCE.

Noor pointed at the line. "I hate that it says my argument better than I do."

Valech answered too.

MERCY OF KALN DEPLOYS COUNTERMEASURE INSIDE WEAPON ENVELOPE.

Jaya cut in. "All units, countermeasure classification rejected unless vector deception, weapon emission, or sensor attack is observed. Record heat telemetry."

Then, privately to Mer: "You are making my shot worse."

Mer answered, "Yes."

"Good."

Sela opened the valves.

The *Mercy* sighed.

It was not loud in command. It was loud in the body. Heat left the old ship in a long controlled exhale, flowing through upper aft radiators and into the debris braid as a red-gold wash on the thermal plot. Mirror skin warmed. Dust lit. The archive reflector spun through the edge of the bloom and became briefly visible to everyone: a broken legal device turning in the heat of a ship refusing to hide.

Valech's targeting cones fuzzed.

Bell's did too.

Harrow Reason reported, "Disabling solution degraded."

Jaya said, "Acknowledged."

Valech said, "Mercy is obstructing lawful restraint."

Tallow Crown logged:

TARGET CERTAINTY DEGRADED BY DECLARED NON-HOSTILE HEAT. OBSTRUCTION CLAIM PRESERVED. HARM REDUCTION CLAIM PRESERVED.

Then Cutter Three moved.

Not much. Enough.

Cho saw it first. "Valech Cutter Three accelerating inward. It will claim the heat bloom threatens medical extraction corridor."

"Does it?" Mer asked.

"No. But if they cross the bloom edge, they can make it look like it did."

Tovin felt the old harmful answer: push the heat harder, force them out, make their lie impossible by making their movement dangerous.

No.

"Cut heat on their side," he said.
